Current Affairs Commentary

Austria's Military Expansion and New Developments in the Central European Question 17

— Ji

European countries have been in a state of military preparation, almost daily, since Germany openly declared its rearmament on March 16th. Britain and France have already implemented military expansion. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, taking advantage of the turbulent European situation, is further expanding his ambitious plans for external development. Italy, Austria, and Hungary also have active plans to complete their military bloc. During the opening of the Anglo-French-Italian Stresa Conference on April 11th, the Italian Prime Minister proudly positioned himself as the leader of Central Europe, proposing the expansion of armaments for Austria and Hungary. Recently, with the establishment of the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact and the rampant rumors of a German-Polish military secret agreement, the division of European military blocs has gradually formed a confrontational situation.

According to a Reuters report, Austria, with the support of Italy, disregards the wishes of the Balkan and Little Entente countries and is implementing its plan to establish an air force, organizing a special domestic defense air corps, with Deputy Prime Minister Steichenburg as the commander-in-chief. This kind of action, which disregards the Treaty of Saint-Germain, is clearly following in Germany's footsteps, dealing a serious blow to the Versailles system.

Examining the Central European question, since the Vienna coup in Austria last year, although it has temporarily achieved stability with the joint support of Italy and France, its underlying crisis has never been eliminated. Germany's attempts to annex Austria are still underway, and the brewing of the restoration of the Habsburg dynasty in Austria has gained considerable support from influential factions. Although the goal has not been achieved due to obstacles in international relations, the hope has never been abandoned. After Germany openly declared its military expansion, members of the Austrian Patriotic Front immediately became active, and calls for the abolition of the Treaty of Saint-Germain spread throughout the country at that time. The Italian Prime Minister, aware of the seriousness of the situation, convened the Rome Conference of Italy, Austria, and Hungary on the 4th of this month, intending to consolidate the union of the three countries, determine specific strategies for dealing with the future Danube River Conference, and serve as the basis for its diplomacy towards France and Germany. However, the outcome of the conference was not significant, and Hungary has already expressed its hesitance, because Hungary feels that its position is vulnerable to German attack and dares not openly join the anti-German bloc. As for the Little Entente and Balkan countries, they immediately became deeply concerned upon hearing the news of Austria's military expansion decision. Therefore, their relationship with Italy has tended to become estranged. Thus, the signatory countries of the Balkan Pact (namely Romania, Yugoslavia, Greece, and Turkey) held a four-nation conference in Rome on the 10th of this month to jointly discuss countermeasures to the international environment. According to official reports, the discussions included: (1) the Mediterranean Pact plan; (2) the mutual relations between the Balkan Entente countries and Italy and the Soviet Union; and (3) the mutual economic relations between the Entente countries. At the same time, close cooperation is being conducted with the Little Entente countries. Former French Foreign Minister Pongou also participated in the conference. Upon closer examination of the truth of the conference, it can be seen that Pongou's participation actually has two roles: (1) France wants to use its position as a mediator to ease the conflict between the Balkan and Little Entente countries and Italy and Austria; (2) France wants to use diplomacy to improve Franco-Italian relations after the establishment of the Franco-Italian agreement. Both of these roles aim to deal with Germany. Now that Austria has implemented military expansion, the situation is quite volatile. Whether the relationship between the Little Entente and Balkan countries and Italy can maintain a peaceful and friendly state is currently uncertain. If the relationship between Italy and the Balkan and Little Entente countries becomes increasingly estranged due to changes in the situation, then the Danube River Nine-Nation Conference, which is about to be convened, will be difficult to proceed smoothly. If so, then France will also face new difficulties in the Central European question due to the futility of its past efforts. All of these are possible effects of Austria's implementation of military expansion plans, which those who pay attention to European issues must not ignore.

The Japanese Foreign Ministry Dispatches Matsushima to Inspect Southwest Asia, Conveying Hirota's Intentions to Overseas Envoys 18

(Tokyo) The Japanese government issued an order today, appointing former Ambassador to Italy, Mr. Hajime Matsushima, as the Foreign Ministry's Second Overseas Inspector, to inspect Southwest Asia and the Near East, and to convey Foreign Minister Hirota's diplomatic policies to Japanese envoys stationed in various places. It is reported that Ambassador Matsushima is scheduled to depart on the 29th and leave Japan from Kobe on the postal ship "Suwa Maru" on the 30th. (Hualian Electric, 16th)

(Tokyo) The countries to be inspected by the Foreign Ministry's first overseas inspector, Ambassador Hajime Matsushima, are as follows: Siam, Iran, Afghanistan, Turkey, India, Ceylon, Hong Kong, British Straits Settlements, and French Annam, etc. (Nichiren Electric, 16th)

France and Russia Resolve to Continue Efforts to Promote the Eastern European Pact; Joint Communiqué Issued After Talks; Stalin Approves of French Defense Policy; Laval to Attend Pilsudski's Funeral in Warsaw 19

(Moscow) French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet leader Molotov held talks for two days, and it is reported that they have agreed to hold a meeting to draft a multilateral pact on consultation and non-aggression, which will be supplemented by mutual assistance pacts signed by countries willing to do so. According to a joint communiqué on the results of the talks, both countries are pursuing the same goal, namely maintaining peace through the organization of universal security. It also stated that the conclusion of the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact does not harm the purpose of establishing an Eastern European regional pact for non-aggression, consultation, and non-assistance to aggressors. The two governments will continue to work to make this pact a success. (Reuters, 15th)

(Moscow) The Franco-Russian talks concluded tonight. French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov issued a joint communiqué, which stated: "The representatives of the two countries advocate continuing negotiations to link the countries that have been considered before, based on the three constraints of mutual non-aggression, mutual consultation, and non-assistance to aggressor countries, to conclude the Eastern European Regional Pact. Stalin, Molotov, and Laval unanimously advocated the organization of collective security to achieve the goal of maintaining peace, and expressed their satisfaction that the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact has generated a spirit of trust between the two countries." The communiqué also stated that the two countries have a responsibility not to allow their defense methods to appear weak. The French national defense policy aims to maintain the military strength of the army to meet the standards of security. Stalin fully understood and completely approved of this policy. The representatives of France and Russia reiterated their determination to support the work of peace building, which can only be fully realized through the cooperation of all related countries in a spirit of freedom and sincerity. If any country is willing to cooperate, France and Russia will never refuse. (Havas, 15th)

(Moscow) During the Moscow talks between Stalin, Molotov, Litvinov, and Laval on May 13, 14, and 15, all expressed satisfaction with the treaty signed in Paris on May 2, 1935, which stipulated the mutual assistance obligations of France and the Soviet Union, and gave a correct interpretation of these obligations. During the review of this treaty, all issues concerning Franco-Soviet relations and the general order of Europe arising from the cooperation plan of the two governments had a beneficial impact. At the same time, it generated a friendly trust between the two countries. The representatives of the Soviet and French sides had the opportunity to state that they were fully and sincerely committed to reviewing, and they firmly believed that the continuous efforts shown by the diplomatic activities of both parties fully demonstrated that they sought only one goal, that is, to maintain peace by organizing collective security. During the exchange of views, they fully agreed that in the current international situation, all those who sincerely maintain peace and have expressed their willingness to jointly establish mutual guarantees should bear the responsibility of maintaining peace. Specifically, they want to maintain peace while never weakening their national defense strength. The French national defense policy aims to maintain a certain military force in accordance with security needs. Stalin expressed full understanding and approval of this point. On the other hand, the representatives of the two countries reiterated their determination that in this long-term cooperation, they will try their best to assist and support governments that support peace policies and create political conditions to restore trust between countries. This kind of trust is necessary for the material and spiritual interests of European countries. The representatives of the two countries reiterated that the conclusion of the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact has not diminished the importance of realizing the Eastern European Regional Pact. This pact will still be worked on by countries that have previously been concerned about it, and the pact contains obligations of mutual non-aggression consultation and non-assistance to aggressor countries. The two governments decided to continue to work together to find diplomatic methods and paths that are most suitable for this goal. The representatives of the Soviet and French sides, in order to publicize the above joint resolutions, made the following full responsibility statement: "The joint efforts are to complete a cause, this cause will not refuse anyone's participation, and the thorough realization of this cause requires the sincere cooperation of all relevant countries." (TASS, 16th)

(Moscow) Judging from the communiqué jointly issued by France and Russia, the two countries have agreed to continue negotiations through diplomatic channels to enable Germany, Poland, and the Soviet Union to jointly conclude the Eastern European Regional Pact, stipulating the obligations of mutual non-aggression, mutual consultation, and non-assistance to aggressor countries between the three countries. The Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact did not intend to encircle Germany and invited Germany to participate. Now, the Franco-Russian communiqué has proposed the conclusion of the Eastern European Regional Pact, so Germany should be even more relieved. If Germany is willing to participate in the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact this time, then European collective security will be enhanced by this organization, and Germany will also benefit from it. (Havas, 15th)

(Paris) Newspapers have commented on the communiqué issued from Moscow. Soviet Communist Party Central Committee General Secretary Stalin's statement in the communiqué approving of French national defense policy is particularly welcomed by newspapers. Only extreme left-wing newspapers expressed dissatisfaction. "Le Petit Parisien" said, "The person who said this is none other than Lenin's successor, the dictator of the Soviet Union, the General Secretary of the Soviet Communist Party, Stalin. This person has great spiritual influence on communists all over the world, including French communists." "Le Matin" is not very trusting of the promises provided by the Soviet government, saying that "If the French Communist Party does not immediately stop anti-militarist propaganda, then the Soviet authorities' prevarication is self-evident." Renowned journalist Bertina published a commentary in "L'Écho de Paris," saying, "Stalin's personal correction of the theory of the French Communist Party is extremely important. There are two reasons for this: (1) The Western European Communist Party has been denied by the Moscow Central Party. The French government only needs to have the courage to easily subdue these propagandists of pacifism (referring to the Communist Party). (2) Stalin has emerged from the mysterious shadows into the world." The Socialist Party's organ newspaper "Le Populaire" said that it is regrettable that the Franco-Russian communiqué did not mention the reduction of armaments. Stalin's approval of French national defense policy is also inappropriate. "The Soviet Union's participation in French domestic affairs was resolutely demanded by Laval. Now that Stalin has stated the reasons for France to organize national defense, those who oppose the two-year conscription system (referring to the French Communist Party) have been publicly criticized by the leader of the Third International. This is the elusive meaning of the Franco-Russian agreement." (Havas, 16th)

French Foreign Minister Departs from Russian Capital; Soviet Dignitaries Give Warm Send-Off 20

(Moscow) French Foreign Minister Laval departed from here tonight to Warsaw to represent the French government at the funeral of Polish General Pilsudski. Foreign Commissar for the People Litvinov and many dignitaries went to the station to see him off. A team of Red Army soldiers lined up to bid farewell, and military bands played the national anthems of France and Russia one after another. The crowd at the station was even larger than when Laval arrived, all cheering and paying their respects. Laval responded with "Long live Franco-Russian friendship." Before departing, Laval went to the opera house to watch a dance drama, and met with Stalin again during the intermission. The conversation was very cordial. At the end of the drama, Laval gave a radio speech, saying, "The coordination between the governments of France and Russia has become closer and closer after the signing of the mutual assistance pact, and the friendship between the two countries has been further consolidated by my visit. My conversations with the leaders of the Soviet government, especially with Mr. Stalin, were extremely candid." Laval then expressed his thanks to the Soviet authorities and people for their warm hospitality, and was very pleased with the results of this trip. (Havas, 15th)

French Delegation Visits the Red Russian Air Force Exercise 21

(Moscow) The Soviet authorities are doing their best to demonstrate to the French delegation the strength of their support for the mutual assistance pact. Yesterday, they inspected factories, military camps, and public works. This morning, they held a large-scale air force review at a military airfield 100 kilometers away from Moscow. It is said that foreign envoys and military attachés have never been allowed to approach the airfield within 30 kilometers. This time, the French reporters accompanying Laval were also allowed to enter the forbidden area to watch the air force exercise. At the most intense moment of the exercise, 24 men and women simultaneously jumped from the same aircraft with safety parachutes. A team of the latest fighter planes flew only a few tens of feet above the ground at a speed of 450 kilometers per hour, passing over the heads of the audience. Laval then congratulated the Air Force Commander on the success. (National News Agency, 16th)

Soviet Union and Czechoslovakia Sign Mutual Assistance Pact; Civil Law, Russia Agreement, and European Peace Add a Link 22

Prague: Representatives of Czechoslovakia and Soviet Russia today signed a mutual assistance treaty here. The content is the same as the Franco-Russian mutual assistance treaty, aiming to prevent the possibility of future wars. This is the result of repeated discussions between Czech Foreign Minister Dr. Benes and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov in the past three weeks. If Germany and Poland still refuse to participate in the Eastern European Pact, then this treaty will replace it. (Reuters, 16th)

Braha: The Soviet-Czech mutual assistance agreement was signed here today, adding another link to European peace. The signatories were Czech Foreign Minister Benes and Soviet Minister to the Czech Republic Aleksandrovsky. The principles of this agreement are the same as the Franco-Russian mutual assistance agreement signed ten days ago. It is generally believed that the conclusion of this agreement is sufficient to strengthen the Soviet Union's western border, which is no less than the Franco-Russian agreement. Therefore, it can not only increase peace in Europe, but also affect the situation in the Far East. Because the Soviet Union has the assistance of France and the Czech Republic, it can reduce Japan's coveting of Russia once it encounters an attack from a European country. Recently, rumors about Germany and Japan brewing an alliance to attack the Soviet Union have been spreading, but German and Japanese diplomats believe that these rumors are not worth refuting. Since the Soviet Union sold the Middle East Railway, Sino-Russian relations have greatly improved. If it can delineate a demilitarized zone in the future, Sino-Russian relations will definitely improve. (National Electric, 16th)

Czech Capital: The Czech-Soviet Union Mutual Assistance Pact was signed today by Foreign Minister Benes and Soviet Ambassador to the Czech Republic Alexandrovsky. The pact is divided into two parts. One part is the mutual assistance treaty, the terms of which are completely the same as the Franco-Soviet Union Mutual Assistance Treaty. The other part is a protocol, which stipulates the scope of application of the mutual assistance treaty. It states that only when the situation stipulated in this treaty occurs, and France implements assistance to the invaded country, will the signatory country assume the obligation of mutual assistance. According to the Czech-Soviet Union Mutual Assistance Treaty, it is related to the Rocarno Convention and supplements the Czech security system. As for the relationship between Czechoslovakia, the Soviet Union, and Poland, it will not be affected by this. (Havas, 16th)

Rumors of British Cabinet Reshuffle Revived, Privy Councilor Baldwin to Succeed as Prime Minister, May Be Realized Before Pentecost, Indian Case Review Completed 25

(London) Rumors of a cabinet reshuffle and a general election in the autumn have now been revived because the Indian case will soon be over. A cabinet reshuffle has long been expected. Prime Minister MacDonald's eye disease has not healed and he is unable to bear the burden of government affairs. He has asked the government to resign for many years. Now there is a normal opportunity to redistribute. It is said that Prime Minister MacDonald and Privy Councilor Baldwin will switch positions during the Pentecost recess. The Indian case is the biggest obstacle to holding a general election. The Indian case should be passed in early August. At that time, the parliament may be dissolved without extending it. Therefore, the rumors of a general election are not unfounded. Supporters of the government believe that holding a general election in October is more beneficial to the government than holding it in the spring of next year. At present, the government's public debt credit is very high, partly because British trade has gradually recovered in the past two years, and partly because of the tense situation in Europe. When the government recently debated in the House of Commons, even the Labor Party, which opposed the government, somewhat supported the government's policy. (Reuters, 15th)

(London) The government's Indian case was submitted to the parliament committee for review. The review was completed last night, which took 30 days. It is unprecedented for the British Parliament to complete the review of such a large project in 30 days. The original case had 450 articles and 15 attachments. After the review, it has increased compared to before. In 30 days, there were 2,000 speeches, totaling 1.5 million words. On average, there were 70 statements of opinion per day. Undersecretary of the Indian Affairs Department, Butler, spoke the most, a total of 200 times. Minister of Indian Affairs, Hall, spoke 166 times. Conservative opposition leader Crawford spoke more than 150 times. Churchill and Minister of Justice Inskip each spoke 100 times. The review committee divided into groups to handle the work, and the progress was very smooth. They made concessions to each other to avoid conflicts of opinion. The third reading of the report will take six days. Then the case can be submitted to the House of Lords. The debate on the third reading of the case will be held around June 4th, 5th, and 2nd. (Reuters, 15th)

The Puppet Manchukuo's Opium Communiqué Creates Astonishment in Geneva: 900,000 Opium Addicts in the Territory, Only 82,600 with Licenses 29

(Geneva) The Puppet Manchukuo Foreign Ministry's Communiqué No. 67, released in Changchun on January 29th of this year, which acknowledges that among the 900,000 opium addicts within its territory, only 82,600 possess licenses, has caused great astonishment here. A spokesperson for the League of Nations' Narcotics Information Bureau stated that, according to the figures in the communiqué, licensed opium smokers constitute only a little less than 10% of the total. The 900,000 addicts in the territory consume approximately 1,642 tons of opium annually, while the 82,600 licensed addicts consume only 51 tons annually. This leaves a staggering 1,491 tons of narcotics outside of regulation. Furthermore, the communiqué states that 7 out of every 1,000 people in the territory smoke processed narcotics, totaling 210,000 people, with an annual consumption of approximately 30 tons. Where these narcotics are manufactured is a matter of great concern. (Central News Agency dispatch, 15th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations' Opium Confiscation Committee today resolved to invite representatives to attend the next meeting to describe the state of the drug trade in the Far East. The Chinese representative, Hu Shih-tse, objected, saying that while he welcomed Japanese cooperation, he questioned the legality of allowing a country that had withdrawn from the League of Nations to participate in this work. He felt that the committee's position did not allow him to express an opinion. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Three British and American Companies Decide to Withdraw Oil Reserves from Manchukuo to Combat the Puppet Regime's Sales Methods 30

(London) Reuters learned today that the three oil companies, Asiatic Petroleum, Socony-Vacuum, and Texaco, have decided to withdraw all of their oil and crude oil reserves from Manchukuo, given the intolerable situation created by the Manchukuo oil monopoly. It is reported that these three companies have applied to the Dalian Customs for a tax refund. Oil company personnel told a Reuters reporter that they have no hope of reaching a compromise and believe that their business in Manchukuo has come to an end. In March 1934, Japan implemented an oil industry law requiring oil companies to maintain large oil reserves in Japan, and granting Japan the right to requisition oil at negotiated prices in times of emergency. The three companies therefore argued to the Japanese government that other countries also made similar demands, but at least bore the expense of building oil storage tanks. It is widely believed that this argument will be effective in securing a satisfactory resolution. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

U.S. Secretary of the Navy Declares: Naval Maneuvers Not Directed at Japan, Nor Testing Aerial Attacks 31

(Washington) Secretary of the Navy Swanson told reporters today that the U.S. fleet's maneuvers in the Pacific are not aimed at Japan. If the Japanese fleet were to conduct maneuvers in the North Pacific without entering within 2,000 miles of the U.S. West Coast, he would not object. Some say that the U.S. fleet is too close to Japanese territory. He emphasized that he has repeatedly ordered U.S. ships not to cross the 180th meridian. In the future, Japanese naval exercises may approach Hawaii even more closely than U.S. ships approach Japan. Hawaii is U.S. territory, but we do not intend to protest, as fleets must have some place to conduct maneuvers. Regarding the statement by Japanese Admiral Kato Kanji that the U.S. naval maneuver site is less than 1,250 miles or ten hours' flight from Japanese territory, he must state categorically that the U.S. naval maneuvers are not intended to test the possibility of aerial attacks. During the maneuvers, the U.S. Navy's main force, while crossing the Pacific from California to Hawaii to deploy its strategy, demonstrated an accuracy and coordination in navigation that was reportedly very satisfying to the command. According to naval authorities, this first phase was a valuable test of naval battle forces operating between widely separated bases. The maneuvers also demonstrated the capabilities of the world's most powerful submarine force. Navy personnel stated that battleships and submarines both performed very well. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Italy Maintains Freedom of Action Regarding Abyssinian Situation; German Veterans Apply to Enlist, Abyssinian Embassy Declines Politely 32

(Rome) According to official sources, Italy intends to maintain complete freedom of action regarding the Abyssinian situation, as the Abyssinian issue is essentially a colonial problem and should not be handled solely within the framework of the League of Nations. It should be considered within the scope of the colonial question. The Fascist government previously supported Abyssinia's entry into the League of Nations, but its intention was to encourage the Abyssinian government to abolish its barbaric practices and join the ranks of civilized nations. However, Abyssinia has not done so, and the Abyssinian government has violated the spirit of the 1928 Italian-Abyssinian treaty. If Italy were to ignore this, it would not only lose its interests but also its prestige as a civilized nation. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

(London) Following Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's speech in the Senate yesterday, explaining the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia, the British press has largely expressed disappointment. The editorial published in this morning's Times is representative, stating: "At a time when the world hopes for a moderation of the situation in East Africa, the Italian Prime Minister's speech was devoid of conciliatory tone. He implied that the prestige of the white race in Abyssinia is in danger of collapsing and that European powers should allow the country to be ravaged." The editorial continues, "While Abyssinian politics are indeed corrupt, the Emperor is a reformer. He is unafraid of criticism as he implements new policies, as has often been the case. Even in the current dispute between Italy and Abyssinia, the Abyssinian Emperor initially suggested submitting the matter to arbitration in accordance with the 1928 bilateral agreement. Both countries had signed a treaty stipulating that disputes should not be resolved by force. Furthermore, regarding the 1906 tripartite agreement between Britain, France, and Italy, the three countries agreed not to interfere in Abyssinia without prior consultation. However, no agreement has been reached between Britain, France, and Italy, and Italy is acting aggressively. Britain and France should therefore exert all their efforts to achieve a peaceful resolution." (Havas dispatch, 16th)

(Berlin) Recently, hundreds of German veterans, radio operators, doctors, and others have arrived at the Abyssinian Consulate General here to offer their services. U.S. Congress Proposes Stabilizing International Currency, Aims to Authorize President to Convene Conference 34

(Washington) Concrete proposals to stabilize the international monetary system have surfaced in Congress today. The proposer is expansionist leader Thomas, who advocates authorizing the President to convene an international monetary conference. However, this proposal has apparently not received the support of the administration. According to the Associated Press, New Deal leaders do not wish to initiate the convening of such a conference, due to the negative experiences the U.S. had during the 1933 London Economic Conference. However, Secretary of State Hull issued a formal statement today, expressing the need for mutual agreement on the current state of the world's monetary systems. According to the State Department's announcement, Hull believes that international monetary stability is an important part of the U.S. foreign trade plan. Therefore, he highly commended Treasury Secretary Morgenthau's speech on Monday evening. Hull did not mention whether an international conference was possible. Hull said, "Unstable exchange rates have indeed caused confusion in the world market, but I believe this is only a transitional situation. The fact that international trade can be maintained in the current difficult circumstances shows that this trade truly meets the real needs of the world. The U.S. is continuing its efforts to restore foreign trade, while also seeking to avoid the impact of exchange rate fluctuations. Many other governments are also adopting this policy. However, extreme manipulation of exchange rates is not a long-term solution, so to expand international trade, we must seek exchange rate stability." (National Dispatch, 15th)

(London) Regarding the U.S. Treasury Secretary's speech on Monday on currency stability and Secretary of State Hull's recent statement that currency stability is an important part of the U.S. trade program, sources here believe that it is purely gratuitous and only seeks to shift the responsibility of initiating negotiations to Britain. Although the statements by American politicians have indeed aroused interest in currency stabilization, British authorities, given the situation in Europe and America, may not be willing to easily accept the responsibility of initiating negotiations. The value of the U.S. dollar, which the British still view as being undervalued in terms of the pound sterling, remains a concern. At the same time, London circles still feel apprehensive about the future of the gold standard, as the difficulties of the French treasury and budget have not been alleviated by the issuance of short-term and long-term bonds in Paris. However, many influential British and American figures believe that the current international trade routes are blocked by quotas and high tariffs. The only way to unclog them is through currency stabilization. One important financier, in a general comment on the current situation, said that although the benefits of currency stabilization are widely recognized, no country is prepared to act first, for fear that other countries will later devalue their currency and gain a trade advantage. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Reuters Important Correction 35

In the May 13th Washington dispatch concerning Secretary of the Treasury Morgenthau's speech, a word was omitted, leading to a misunderstanding of the meaning. The original cable read, "Why do people uniquely choose to admonish the U.S.? Restoring order is our moral responsibility." It should have read, "Why do people uniquely choose to admonish the U.S. to restore order as our moral responsibility?"

15-Year-Old Japanese Boy Attempts Solo Voyage, Secretly Boards Yacht and Casts Off from Yokohama Port, Eventually Overcome by Seasickness and Helplessness 36

(Tokyo) A 15-year-old Japanese boy, Ishida, driven by curiosity, attempted to sail from Yokohama to Singapore. Last night, he secretly boarded a yacht moored in Yokohama port and, after a fifteen-minute interval, cast off. He hoped for a smooth sailing to his destination. This morning, Lieutenant Commander Master, a military attaché at the French Embassy in Tokyo, discovered that his yacht was missing and immediately reported it to the Water Police Bureau. Shortly after the search began, the ship was found floating several miles outside Yokohama port. By this time, Ishida had lost heart and, though no longer concerned with life or death, was suffering terribly from seasickness. There had been a strong wind the previous night, and Ishida, unfamiliar with sailing techniques, was helpless. Although he tried to steer back to Yokohama, he was unable to and allowed the ship to drift. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

National Government Revises Domestic Travel Expense Regulations 40

(Nanjing) The National Government announced on the 16th the revised domestic travel expense regulations, totaling twelve articles. The key points are as follows: (1) These regulations shall apply to all personnel traveling on official business within the country, except for those with special circumstances requiring separate travel expense regulations. (2) Travel expenses are divided into transportation, accommodation and miscellaneous expenses, and special expenses. Except for the Chairman of the National Government, members of the National Government, and the presidents and vice-presidents of the five Yuan, who are reimbursed for actual expenses, all others shall be paid according to their current rank, in accordance with: (A) Transportation: specially appointed and senior appointments first class, recommended and delegated appointments second class, employees, laborers, and attendants third class; (B) Accommodation and miscellaneous expenses (calculated daily): specially appointed 18 yuan, senior appointment 12 yuan, recommended appointment 8 yuan, delegated appointment 6 yuan, employees 4 yuan, laborers and attendants 2 yuan; (C) Special expenses are reimbursed for actual expenses, as specified above. However, in special circumstances, such as handling foreign affairs or entertaining foreign guests, the required travel expenses may be reimbursed for actual expenses. (3) After the completion of the business trip, a detailed, itemized, and daily travel expense report, along with a travel diary, shall be submitted to the head of the respective agency for approval within fifteen days, attached to the receipt book and sent to the Audit Department for review. (4) Transportation expenses shall be paid according to fixed rates. However, if transportation is provided by the government or a free pass is obtained, no expenses shall be claimed. Those with half-price tickets may be reimbursed for half the price. In areas with inconvenient transportation, the necessary boat, vehicle, and sedan chair expenses shall be reimbursed for actual expenses. (5) Special expenses include postage, telegraph, and expenses for temporary hiring of laborers, vehicles, and horses, as well as all other necessary expenses incurred for official business. (6) Personnel traveling on official business who must bring attendants shall be limited to two for specially appointed personnel and one each for senior, recommended, and delegated appointees, unless there are special circumstances. (7) These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 16th)

International Commercial Telegram - Reuters Special Business Report, May 16 51

Gold and Silver

British Gold: London gold prices fell two pence due to the rise in the pound, to 142 shillings and 7 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market was stable today. Silver prices rose by 1.25, with spot prices at 35.275 pence and futures at 35.5625 pence. China bought, India sold, and speculators engaged in both buying and selling. Market sentiment at the close was uncertain.

American Silver: The Mountrie silver market opened higher today, in sympathy with the London market. There was a significant price difference between buyers and sellers.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning, with minimal price fluctuations. The pound sterling showed a slightly stronger trend. The opening exchange rate for British pounds to U.S. dollars was 4.87875, the same as the previous day's closing price for U.S. dollars to British pounds. It rose to 4.88 within the first hour and continued to rise by 0.003125 at noon to 4.883125. It remained unchanged at 1:00 PM and rose again by 0.001875 at 2:00 PM to 4.885.

British-French: The opening rate was 74.06 francs, 3 centimes higher than yesterday's close. It fell 2 centimes within the first hour and rebounded by 11 centimes at noon to 74.15 francs. It fell 5 centimes at 1:00 PM to 74.10 francs and rebounded by 6 centimes at 2:00 PM to 74.16 francs.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: New York cotton prices opened slightly lower, and trading was sluggish. Then there was a trend to rise with the stock market. Industry purchases were also higher than before. The weather in the cotton-growing region is reportedly quite cold with continuous rain, so some cotton fields now need to be replanted. Merchants are waiting for the results of the Tariff Commission's investigation into the manufacturing costs of cotton goods and expect Washington to impose import duties on cotton goods or change the cotton goods handling fees.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was stable today. The price for July futures at 1:00 PM was 6.51, the same as the previous day's closing price.

British Wheat: Prices in the Liverpool wheat market rose slightly today. The price for July futures at 1:00 PM was 5 shillings and 5.375 pence, up half a penny from yesterday's close.

Wheat: Although there were reports of continued rain in the wheat-growing region, the Chicago wheat market opened higher today, expressing sympathy with the prices of other crops. Prices continued to be strong after the opening, and prices of miscellaneous grains also rose quickly, despite the fact that Argentina has sufficient grain for export, but prices still fell. It is reported that planting has been delayed due to rain.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was stable today. The trading prices for July and September futures at noon were 6.0625 pence. New York: The New York rubber market continued to show more bullish sentiment today. Opening prices rose 12 centimes and showed a firm trend. It is predicted that statistical positions will gradually increase again.

Securities

New York: At the beginning of trading today, there was a general upward trend because supporters of the Patman Bonus Bill are expected to gather sufficient support to override President Roosevelt's veto. The inflationary implications of this bill have driven up the prices of various securities, and other news has also boosted buying sentiment. General Motors can fully resume production within a week, and the Public Utility Holding Company Act can also stabilize the market prices of public utility company securities. Silver mining stocks rose first, and railroad stocks also showed good demand. The prices are as follows:

Ministry of Finance Orders Three Provinces and Cities to Abolish Harsh Taxes 52

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, noting that Zhejiang, Hebei, and Tianjin still have some harsh and miscellaneous taxes, has ordered their abolition. These include: (A) Zhejiang: (1) The Finance Department presented to the Provincial Government for approval the establishment of a "Wealthy Monk Donation"; (2) Yellow Sand Tax; (3) Silk and Ramie Improvement Fee. The "Wealthy Monk Donation" is a tax levied based on the amount of property of each temple. The Yellow Sand Tax is levied on both wholesale and retail sales. The Silk and Ramie Improvement Fee requires silk and ramie merchants to deposit cash, paying a certain amount per certain weight of ramie sold. (B) Hebei's Caoxian County: In addition to taxes levied at the market, meat shops, and on slaughtered livestock, there is also a "Market Foundation Inspection Tax". Furthermore, pig bristles, pig hair, pig blood, and other items are all owned by the market and subject to a monopoly, requiring a tax of three yuan per pig. (C) Tianjin: The brokerage tax is collected in excess of the prescribed amount. (Sixteenth Day Special Dispatch)

The Commander of the Fake Fujian-Jiangxi Region, Song Yuanquan, Captured; High-Ranking Members of Song's Band Captured; Remnants Fleeing to Dehua Still Being Surrounded and Suppressed 91

Xiamen Correspondence: Song Yuanquan, the commander of the fake Fujian-Jiangxi Military Region (also known as Zheng Hanqi), was a remnant of Fang Zhimin's troops. The band had fake regiments such as the 12th, 17th, 18th, and 19th, and harassed northern Fujian. After Wei Lihuang, Li Moan, and others sent teams to suppress them, the bandits fled through Qingliu, Ninghua, Youxi, and Sha County, entering Guilin in Datian. They were intercepted by the 9th Security Regiment. Song led the fake 12th and 19th regiments, totaling more than 600 people, and fled to Liuyuan between Xianyou and Yongtai. They were already close to the coastal plain, like entering a dead end with no way out. In addition, they were hungry and exhausted. Lin Chong and Wang Zhigang of the Xianyou Security Brigade lured them to Duwei Town, providing them with food and clothing. Song, in dire straits, surrendered to the Xianyou County Government. Lin and Wang, together with Song and the fake Chief of Staff Xu Jianghan, went to the county town on the 9th to negotiate, and then went to Duwei with Deng Jun, the director of the screening department, to inspect. At that time, the Quanzhou Third Pacification Command, based on a report, dispatched the 49th and 50th regiments of the 25th Brigade of the 9th Division to Xianyou, and disarmed all the bandits, capturing more than 600 people and more than 400 rifles. Not a single one escaped. Song Yuanquan, Xu Jianghan, and fifteen other officers, including Peng Hu, the fake director of the political department, Wu Jinren and Zhang Tianquan, the fake battalion commanders, Wang Weisheng and Zuo Longwu, the fake political commissars, Zhou Yi, Yang Liangsheng, and Zhang Xiangbiao, the fake company instructors, Su Huawei, Ruan Douyuan, Yang Zhikun, and Yu Longsheng, the fake company adjunct instructors, and Jiang Cuiying (female), the fake local work team, were all arrested. According to Song, the 12th and 19th regiments under his command had about 1,400 people. Because they were surrounded on all sides by the National Army in the bandit area (between Jianning and Ninghua), they could not stand their ground, so they marched secretly at night, leaving the bandit area, passing through Guihua, Qingliu, Youxi, and Datian, and arriving in Xianyou. They were intercepted by the National Army along the way, leaving only six or seven hundred people and four or five hundred guns. Later, they learned that the 9th Division had sent troops to surround and suppress them in Yongxian, and they had no way to go, so they rushed to the Xianyou County Government to request surrender. However, Zhong Xunren, the fake political commissar and secretary of the military region, led dozens of members of the fake regimental headquarters and fled back to the bandit area, and so on. Song and the other fifteen people were escorted to the Quanzhou Pacification Command on the 14th and will be transferred to the Zhangzhou Pacification Headquarters. As for the fake 17th and 18th countries, they are being pursued very closely by Yang's regiment of the 83rd Division. They fled to Chishui in Dehua on the 11th and were blocked by the 9th Security Regiment and the 52nd Division. They were surrounded on all sides on Shantouping on the 12th, and the solution should not be far away. (May 16)

Zichuan: Tragic Disaster at the Luda Mine: More Than 800 Miners, More Than 600 Dead 92

Jinan Correspondence: According to a special report from Zichuan, at about 11 AM on the 13th of this month, at the Zichuan Hongshan Sino-Japanese joint venture Luda Company mine, the hole cover suddenly collapsed, and the old, abandoned, and empty water broke through the stones that had been blocked the hole and rushed out. In less than half an hour, the cave water had filled the tunnels. In addition, the electric water pumps exploded when they came into contact with the water, making pumping difficult. Therefore, the water grew stronger and larger. There were about 800 miners in the pit working. No more than 200 people escaped. The remaining 600 people were blocked in the pit by the water. As of 10 PM on the 14th, a long-distance telephone call was received from Zichuan, which said that the factory was rescuing and pumping water, and Zichuan County Magistrate and Garrison Commander Ning were maintaining order at the scene. The families of the workers who were broken into pieces heard the news and all went to the mine to inquire about the news, gathering outside the door and crying loudly. The situation was extremely tragic, a rare disaster in recent years. The details of the various situations are recorded below:

Luda's Evolution: Since the Cao County religious case occurred in the former Qing Dynasty, the Qing government and the Germans signed the Jiaozhou Bay lease treaty, which included a mining item. In the 27th year of Guangxu (1901), the Germans organized the German-Chinese Company to mine minerals in Fangzi, Jinling Town, Zichuan and other places. When the European War broke out, the Germans' power to plunder was transferred to the Japanese. After seven years, at the Washington Conference in the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the Sino-Japanese Luda Company was organized based on the treaty. The Zichuan coal mine is part of the company, named the Zichuan Mining Office of Luda Company, about four miles southeast of Zichuan City, in a place called Hongshan, commonly known as Dahuangdi. Luda calls itself the main pit of the Zichuan Mining Office. The current director is Japanese Ichikichi Tetsuo, and the associate director and standing director, vice director is Chinese Song Biru.

Organization Below the Pit: The Luda Zichuan Mining Office mine has two wells, north and south. The south well is larger in scale and has important machinery. Currently, the north well has a richer output and the coal washing stove is larger than the south well, so coal is currently produced in the north well. The pit tunnels are divided into two roads, eight layers and ten layers. From the ground to the eighth layer, it is 180 meters deep (about 50 zhang). Lifting and lowering are purely powered by steam. From the eighth layer to the tenth layer, up and down are powered by electricity, a distance of 320 meters from the ground (about 90 zhang). Underground travel is purely by electric car. Some tunnels are more than a dozen miles long. The average monthly coal output of the main and outer pits of Luda is about 2,000 tons. In addition to the 14 tons required by the Jiaoji Railway, most of it is sold in Shanghai, Qingdao and other places.

Circumstances of the Disaster: The sturdiness of the tunnel project in the mine has a direct relationship with the lives of the miners. Therefore, the factory's saving of labor and materials is not only opposed by the workers, but also prohibited by the factory law. The death rate of Luda has always been higher than other mines. The tragedy that occurred this time is said to be due to the mine's recent removal of all the coal pillars in the tunnel. Since the Japanese Ichikichi and the Chinese Song Biru took office, they replaced most of the old people in the mine and cleared out all the coal pillars in the mine. At about 11 AM on the 13th of this month, the stones on the top floor of the tenth layer in the mine were washed away by water. At the same time, the 74th abandoned flood water destroyed the plug stones. In less than half an hour, each road was blocked. The electric water pumps were stepped up to pump water. In fear, there was another explosion. Therefore, the water became more and more increased. If the miners working in the tenth floor wanted to get out of the well, they had to pass through the eighth floor before they could reach the top. At this time, a total of more than 800 people were submerged together. Ning Chunxiao, the brigade commander of the 64th Brigade stationed in Zichuan, and Zhang Yunzao, the county magistrate, rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm and dispatched troops and husbands to assist the Luda Company in rescuing the submerged workers and maintaining order. They rescued only more than 200 people. It is not yet known whether the remaining 600 people were drowned in the well or were calling to find other places to avoid the water. However, it is really difficult to get out of danger for a while.

In the Rescue: Most of the miners are residents of nearby areas. When the families heard the news, they were all frightened and gathered outside the gate of the mine to inquire about the news. They all believed that it was more ominous than auspicious and cried loudly. Tonight, this reporter inquired about the news by long-distance telephone. It was said that the water had not yet receded, and the mine was trying to find a way to rescue the workers, stepping up efforts to pump water outwards. It was also said that the water could be completely pumped out a week later. It is still difficult to predict whether these 600 people can be rescued. It is really an unprecedented tragedy in the coal mines of Shandong Province.

Another News: Zichuan Telegram. At 11:25 AM on the 13th, a large amount of water suddenly occurred at the No. 75 coal mining place in the second vertical pit of Luda Zichuan. The water was turbulent and the traffic was cut off. For about 40 minutes, although there was a water pump, the water pump could not move due to the water filling the bottom of the well, losing its effectiveness. About 400 workers under the kiln, as well as Japanese engineer Aihara Zōzō and surveyor Yuan Rongfang, are unknown. The Chinese and Japanese staff of the company, although they tried their best to rescue, but all the dozen or so water pumps were not applicable, and they were extremely anxious. The water rose higher and higher, but they could only wail helplessly. By the evening, they had not been able to rescue anyone. On the 8th, the tunnel was unable to ventilate due to carbonic acid gas, and there were about 200 workers above the 19th coal mining place who had not been rescued. The company reported to the company's important staff in Qingdao on the one hand, and organized a death squad to go down to the kiln to rescue on the other hand. However, due to excessive gas, they could not approach. After the Luda vertical pit was flooded, the water rose one meter per hour. By 3 AM on the 14th, it was only 18 meters from the wellhead, and the first vertical pit was also in great danger. According to the usual practice, water gushes out from the bottom of the well in coal pits, so workers can escape. The Luda tragedy this time was actually caused by the sudden outbreak of a large amount of water in the middle of the well, causing hundreds of workers to be unable to escape. Now that the water pumps in the well cannot be used, new water pumps have been urgently purchased to pump water outside the well to salvage hundreds of remains. It is said that it will take about a week to salvage them. (15th)

Shanxi Discoveries of Ancient Shang and Zhou Artifacts; Rumors of Private Sales by Corrupt Officials and Gentry; Antiquities Preservation Committee Sends Letter to Inquire 93

Beijing Dispatch: It has come to light that ancient Shang and Zhou artifacts were recently discovered in Hunyuan County, Shanxi Province. There are now rumors that these artifacts are being sold to foreign merchants. The Beijing office of the Antiquities Preservation Committee has sent a letter to local gentry in the county to investigate the truth. The original letter stated (excerpts omitted): "We recently received a document transferred from the National Palace Museum in Beijing, which states that the Shang and Zhou bronzes unearthed in Hunyuan are truly rare treasures. It would be a great pity if they were dispersed. Our office is responsible for their preservation and cannot allow corrupt officials and gentry to freely dispose of them. We are unsure whether they are still within the country. Could you please ascertain the current address of the former county magistrate, Yuan Xinghua, and report the dates of the discovery and the process of the illicit sales, providing factual information. It would be best if you could come to Beijing in person to explain." (excerpts omitted)

Previously, on the evening of the thirteenth day of the first month of the old lunar calendar in the twelfth year of the Republic [1923], Gao Fengshan, a villager from Dongyu Village, fifteen li southwest of Hunyuan County, discovered ancient artifacts in his farmland. He then exerted his strength to excavate them. Aside from gold and jade items, the finds consisted entirely of ancient bronzes. Gao Fengshan, being a farmer, initially did not know that these were valuable antiques. He gradually dispersed them, keeping only the ones that were easy to sell. News of the bronze artifacts then reached a Mr. Yu, who purchased some. This caused a sensation. The then-magistrate of Hunyuan County, Xie Encheng, upon hearing of this matter, immediately ordered the county police officer Zuo Chengwei to go to Dongyu to investigate. Aside from what Gao Fengshan had kept, they obtained a total of thirty-six sets, large and small, which were temporarily displayed in the county library.

Around the thirteenth and fourteenth years of the Republic [1924-1925], antique dealers from Beijing and Tianjin heard the news and flocked to appraise them. A French merchant offered 40,000 yuan, but the deal was put on hold due to the Yan-Feng War. At that time, general epigraphers were unable to determine which dynasty the artifacts were from. In the fifteenth year of the Republic [1926], a certain county gentleman purchased them for 40,000 yuan, but only paid a small portion of the money at the time, agreeing to pay the remainder by the eighteenth year of the Republic [1929]. Unexpectedly, the gentleman passed away the following year, and his son inherited the property, halting the payments. It was not until the twenty-first year of the Republic [1932] that the county gentry intervened and retrieved the artifacts. A Mr. Ma identified them as ritual vessels from the Shang and Zhou dynasties, of great value. Subsequently, antique dealers from Beijing offered 100,000 yuan to purchase them, but the offer was rejected. Therefore, the gentry and scholars of the county agreed that they would not sell them for less than 500,000 yuan. As a result, even an offer of 300,000 yuan was not accepted. Currently, the Antiquities Preservation Committee is paying close attention to the progress of this matter. There are rumors that the artifacts may be transported to Taiyuan or sold privately. Meanwhile, the gentry of Hunyuan County are appealing to all parties for assistance. (13th)

Songjiang Typhoon Destroys Seawall 94

The Jinshanwei (Tuolin) area in the eighth district of this county is coastal and has a seawall to protect the inland. During the typhoon in the eleventh year of the Republic [1922], it was once destroyed. With the approval of the provincial authorities, the former Director of Construction Bureau, Xu Baikui, allocated funds to repair it using new methods. Recently, it was hit by another strong typhoon, causing sections four and six of the seawall to be washed away for tens of zhang, scattered in disarray, with a total length of over a hundred zhang, which is extremely dangerous. The Seawall Engineering Bureau reported this to the county government for review. County Magistrate Jin, upon receiving the report, took a car with the head of the Construction Section, Xu Mojia, to Jinshanwei yesterday (15th) to inspect the damage. They then went to Shanyang to check on the baojia system before returning to Songjiang in the evening.

"Great Songjiang Daily" Sued 95

Recently, the Yang Ji Opium Shop in the city was reported for harboring prostitutes.陆建芬 Lu Jianfen, a patrol officer from the First Precinct, led police to arrest a man and a woman. The next day, the local "Great Songjiang Daily" reported the incident, stating that the captured female patron, a local prostitute named Zhang Pinxian, was the daughter of a Mr. Yang from Dongwai, named Yang Pinguan. Mr. Yang claimed that although he had once had an adopted daughter, she had been expelled long ago, and the arrested Zhang Pinxian was completely unrelated. He sent a letter to the newspaper requesting a correction, but the newspaper received a registered letter containing blank white paper with no words. The newspaper's editor deemed it suspicious and reported it to the Public Security Bureau and published a statement in an advertisement. Yang Jinbiao, believing that the newspaper had not made a legally required correction, considered it a public insult and filed a lawsuit in the county court, seeking legal action. It is reported that the court has scheduled a hearing for the twenty-third.

Qingpu Murder of Husband Case in Songbin Township 96

Jiang Yuezhen, a young woman from Xiaozhangjia Village in Songbin Township, the sixth district of Qingpu, is currently 24 years old. She married Jiang Aisheng from the neighboring Jiwangmiao Township as her husband when she was 15 years old. They married at 19, and their relationship was still harmonious. However, recently, due to the increasingly difficult financial situation of the family, the relationship between husband and wife gradually deteriorated. Zhang Aquan, a young man from the same village, also 24 years old, saw that the couple was not on good terms and began to seduce her. Within two months, they became intimate. As a result, the relationship between Yuezhen and her husband deteriorated further. The other night, Aisheng suddenly hanged himself. Jiang Renshe, Yuezhen's cousin, reported to the head of the sixth district, Zhu, that Aisheng had hanged himself for no reason, requesting the arrest of the murderer and legal action. After receiving the report, District Head Zhu sent the police to the village to arrest the suspected murderers Zhang Aquan and Jiang Yuezhen, and telegraphed the county government to send officials to inspect the body. At ten o'clock this morning, Shen Yuankai, a trial officer sent by the county, and the forensic official Zhen, went to the village to inspect the body. The results showed a fist wound on the left arm, black marks on the fingernails and toes, and redness on the testicles, indicating that he had been beaten before hanging himself. The corpse was claimed by the family for burial. The two suspects, by District Head Zhu, was on the same day prepared with documents and sent to the county government for verification.

Suzhou Embezzlement Case in Land Tax Collection to Be Expanded 97

The case of Zhu Xijun, the former director of the Land Tax Collection Office of the county government, accused of dereliction of duty, embezzlement, and misappropriation of over ten thousand dollars of public funds, has been widely reported. Dong Binqian, sent by the Finance Department, came to Suzhou to investigate, but the case has been pending for a year without resolution. It is now heard that after Dong investigated the case, he believed that there was corruption in the wasteland reclamation in the twentieth year of the Republic [1931], with over 40,000 yuan of public funds being misappropriated by Zhu. There were also irregularities in the advance borrowing of grain before the sixteenth year of the Republic [1927], and conclusive evidence has been found. After reporting to Director Zhao, Wu County Magistrate was ordered to order Zhu to pay off 40,000 yuan of public funds within five days before being investigated. As of yesterday, the five-day deadline has expired, and Zhu Xijun has refused to pay. Wu County Magistrate has submitted a report to the Finance Department for instructions. It is heard that this case may be expanded, and Zhu may be sent to the province for trial. It is also said that the case may be transferred to the judiciary.

Wuxi Juvenile Fighting Leads to Death 98

The Wu Gonghe Yi Firecracker Shop outside the North Gate Tantu Bian is owned by Wu A'gen. The firecracker factory is located at No. 17 Zhang Lane near Chang'an Bridge. Zhu Jinhe, a sixteen-year-old apprentice from Jingjiang, was introduced to the shop at the age of eleven. He was due to complete his apprenticeship in August of this year. The apprentice lived in a small loft in the workshop. However, he was very mischievous and often formed gangs with nearby children to fight. On the fifth of this month, Jinhe and more than ten Jiangbei children, including Zhao A'ju, had a fight. Because he was outnumbered, he was beaten and injured. On the twelfth, he developed a fever and complained of pain, unable to get out of bed. He died from his injuries the day before yesterday. The head of the district, Wu Rongmo, and the owner of the shop, Wu Xilin, reported to the local branch court, requesting an autopsy. Upon receiving the report, Prosecutor Shen, accompanied by forensic official Wang, went to perform the autopsy. The autopsy revealed a fatal fist wound on the left rib, indicating that he had died from his injuries suffered a few days earlier. The shop owner was ordered to prepare a coffin for burial. The murderers Zhao A'ju, Su Rinnian, and Hu A'san were apprehended by the shop owner and sent to the Fifth Sub-Bureau for questioning.

Letter to the Editor 99

Dear Mr. Reporter,

We are writing to you regarding a news item concerning our office published in your newspaper on the tenth of this month, which contains some inaccuracies. We hereby list them below and request that you correct them. Sincerely, General Affairs Section, Shanghai Municipal Audit Office of the Audit Department.

Original text: The fifteenth of each month is the audit day.

Correction: According to central government regulations, all agencies must prepare their income and expenditure statements no later than the fifteenth day of the following month. It is not the fifteenth that is the audit day.

Original text: All agencies below the National Government must submit their various relief registers to the Audit Office for review on that day.

Correction: According to the authority of this office, all agencies under the municipal government and central agencies in Shanghai are subject to our audit duties. Not all agencies below the National Government are audited by this office.

Shi Family Funeral Held Yesterday; Memorial Service Held by Newspaper Staff This Morning 100

Yesterday was the day of the family funeral for the late General Manager of this newspaper, Mr. Shi Liangcai. All the staff of this newspaper specifically held a public memorial service yesterday morning. Around ten o'clock, more than four hundred people arrived at the Shi residence at No. 257 Hartung Road. At 11:10, Gu Angruo rang the bell, and the colleagues gathered in the mourning hall to begin the public memorial service amid mournful music. The order was as follows: (1) The chief mourner took his place, (2) the assisting mourners took their places, (3) the participants took their places, (4) the chief mourner offered incense and sacrificial silk, (5) the participants stood in silence, (6) the eulogy was read, (7) the entire group paid their respects, (8) the ceremony was completed.

Zhang Yunhe, the chief editor of this newspaper, officiated at the reading of the eulogy. Zhou Mengxiong, the deputy chief editor, Ma Yinliang, the manager, and Huating assisted in the memorial. After the chief mourner offered incense and sacrificial silk, the participants stood in silence, and Qian Hua read the eulogy, saying: "On the sixteenth day of May in the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China [1935], all the staff of the Shen Bao, Zhang Yunhe and others, reverently offer clear wine and various delicacies to the spirit of the late General Manager Shi Liangcai, saying: 'Oh, our respected gentleman, receiving your mandate from Heaven, you have rendered great service, diligently working throughout the years, extensively informed and upright, with comprehensive understanding, broad application, and abundant talent, you have been successful in all endeavors. You excel in eloquence, moving with ease and skill, resolving disputes with a few words, and inspiring admiration. Diligently striving, speaking frankly and openly, you have supported municipal administration, promoting peace and tranquility. Lamenting the darkness of the times and the prevalence of turmoil, you have carefully considered popular sentiments, expressing opinions on current affairs. Distinguishing between right and wrong, unwavering in your principles, clearing obstacles and boldly leading the way. Why has Heaven not favored the virtuous, allowing such disaster to befall a righteous man? Your loyal blood, shed unjustly, evokes eternal sorrow. Especially for us, who have long been under your protection, hearing of your passing fills us with grief and loss. We will continue your aspirations and carry on your work, planning for the future. Although you are gone, your resolute spirit will always be with us. We will follow your standards and never slacken or falter. Remembering those guilty, who are still at large, your resentment in the netherworld causes you ceaseless anxiety. We offer spices and medicine, declaring our sorrow at your spirit banner. As you ride the stars, may you come and accept our offerings. Alas!'" At twelve o'clock, the ceremony was completed, and the colleagues dispersed one after another.

Dedication of the Memorial Tablet in the Afternoon: At five o'clock in the afternoon, the ceremony for dedicating the memorial tablet was held. Huang Zanxi served as the chief guest, with Zhu Shouchun and Feng Yangshan assisting. Jia Jiying was the master of ceremonies. The ceremony was extremely solemn. After nine o'clock in the evening, the family memorial began. Today, invitation cards, plain carriages, and white horses are expected to create a grand spectacle.

Chairman Lin to Return to Nanjing; Visited the Lake Society Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition Yesterday 101

Chairman Lin came to Shanghai this time to invite Doctors Lu Zhong'an and Lin Zuhan to treat his stomach problems and dental ailments. He has been progressing well in recent days. According to those at the Lin residence, the Chairman is expected to stay in Shanghai for about three or four more days, and his return to Nanjing is expected around the twentieth.

National Government Chairman Lin has recovered his health. At 8:30 yesterday morning, he traveled lightly and simply to the Lake Society on Guizhou Road to visit the Six-Ying Hall Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition, which was being held at the Lake Society. He selected more than ten items, including a couplet handwritten by Zhang Zixiang and a hanging scroll of flowers painted by Empress Dowager Cixi of the Qing Dynasty. Afterwards, the general manager of the society, Ling Songru, welcomed him to the reception room on the second floor. After exchanging pleasantries, he presented the "Lake Society Remembering the Worthies" scroll painted by the famous calligrapher Fei Xiaolou, which depicted fifteen officials from the Jiajing era of the Ming Dynasty, with calligraphy by the late calligrapher Bao Zizhuang. The procurement of machinery for the two plants will also be undertaken by the company, and it is currently in contact with various parties, intending to adopt bidding procedures. He visited as a member of the Special Education Committee, so the inspection was entirely based on education. Due to the banditry in various places, the wounds were deeply rooted, and there were very few able-bodied men. It is necessary to work hard on education and training. After the inspection, he went to Hankou to inspect the business of the National Goods Bank branch, which has been quite prosperous recently.

Promoting Literacy Education: Citywide Mobilization Yesterday; Each Group Carries Forms to Survey Households; Survey to Be Completed in Two Weeks 109

The Municipal Literacy Education Committee, in order to promote literacy education, was instructed by the municipal government to eliminate illiteracy within one year in order to enlighten the people. Yesterday was a citywide mobilization, and each group took the survey forms and a page of paper with six hundred characters and set off to investigate each month. The investigation was divided into (1) no literacy, (2) half literacy, (3) four-sixths literacy. The survey procedure is limited to completion within two weeks. The Literacy Education Committee also issued a notice to residents, asking them to report truthfully for statistics and to prepare for the establishment of literacy schools.

Telephone Fee Increase Postponement Case: Negotiations Underway, Public Works Committee of the Municipal Council Accepts Meeting Minutes 110

The Public Works Committee of the Municipal Council convened a meeting on May 10th to discuss the telephone company's request for a telephone fee increase and the issue of telephone charges in the Chinese-administered areas of Shanghai. The minutes of the meeting were submitted to the Municipal Council's board meeting this past Wednesday. Regarding the issue of telephone charges in the Chinese-administered areas, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, based on requests from taverns and 37 other organizations, requested the cancellation of the five-cent telephone charge in the Chinese-administered areas, arguing that since they are all within the same city of Shanghai, telephone charges should not be levied separately, as this hinders business. The telephone company refuted this, stating that the charge was based on a contract signed on December 19, 1925, between the Chinese authorities and the Shanghai Telephone Company and has been collected since the contract was signed. Moreover, the so-called "Cross-Boundary Road Construction Contract" signed between the Chinese Telephone Bureau and the Shanghai Telephone Company on April 19, 1933, also included this point, arguing that given Shanghai's vast urban area, wouldn't it be appropriate to levy extra telephone charges, as is done in New York and London? When the Public Works Committee discussed this matter, the secretary stated that telephone charges in the Chinese-administered areas should be determined by the two telephone authorities in the Chinese areas. Only if the charge is cancelled and telephone fees in the foreign-administered areas must be increased to compensate the telephone company's losses would this be a matter for the Municipal Council. It was noted that of the five-cent charge, three cents went to the Shanghai Telephone Company and two cents to the Chinese Telephone Bureau. The accountant and administrator stated that telephone charges in the Chinese-administered areas were an important source of revenue for the telephone company, and they believed that this case should be discussed after the issue of telephone fees within the foreign-administered areas is resolved. During the discussion, it was generally agreed that according to telephone statistics, the number of calls from the Chinese-administered areas was greater, so the benefits to telephone subscribers in the Chinese-administered areas were actually greater than those in the foreign-administered areas. The committee lacked the authority to change the contract signed by both parties. The committee should call the telephone company's attention to the fallacy of levying telephone charges in the Chinese-administered areas, but the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce should provide special evidence. The committee suggested to the Municipal Council that this case should be postponed until a decision is made on the telephone fee increase in the foreign-administered areas. Next, the issue of the telephone fee increase in the foreign-administered areas was discussed. The secretary presented a memorandum on this issue and the process of the telephone company's request for a fee increase. On April 18th, the foreign ratepayers' annual meeting passed a resolution requesting the Municipal Council to renegotiate with the telephone company, postpone the fee increase, and organize a special telephone committee to allow sufficient time to discuss this case. On May 8th, the telephone company requested approval of the May bills, which were consistent with April. The issue lies in the Municipal Council's responsibility for the telephone company's losses starting from April, as the Council is responsible for delaying the implementation of the new telephone rates starting April 1st. The committee recommended to the Municipal Council that it approve the company's request for May bills to be consistent with April. Regarding the resolution passed by the foreign ratepayers' annual meeting, the committee observed that it could be divided into two points: "(1) The Municipal Council should begin negotiations with the telephone company to postpone the fee increase; (2) Organize a special telephone committee and invite one or more experts to join the committee." The Public Works Committee strongly supports negotiating with the telephone company. When the Municipal Council discussed the committee's recommendations, it was stated that informal negotiations were underway. The Municipal Council approved the proposal to formally negotiate with the telephone company to postpone the fee increase and passed the Public Works Committee's meeting minutes in their entirety.

According to the Shanghai Times, on Tuesday (the 14th), customs patrol boats seized a large Fujian-style civilian vessel suspected of smuggling outside the Wusongkou. Amidst Anti-Chinese Sentiment in Siam, Siamese Representative Mr. Swardt Arrives in China, Currently in Japan, Expected to Arrive in Shanghai on the 21st to Investigate Trade Conditions and Conduct Treaty Negotiations 112

The Ta Kung Pao reports that since overseas Chinese in Siam were illegally oppressed by the Siamese government, they dispatched representatives to form a petition delegation to return to China, requesting negotiations with the central government and appealing to various organizations to implement a boycott of Siamese rice imports. Sino-Siamese relations suddenly became strained. To understand the situation in China and negotiate a treaty, the Siamese authorities specially sent Customs Tax Commissioner Mr. Swardt to China to investigate trade conditions and to negotiate a commercial treaty with the Chinese government. While passing through Japan, he exchanged informal opinions with Mr. Jiang Zuobin, the Chinese Ambassador to Japan. Yesterday, the Siamese commercial organization stationed in Shanghai received a telegram from Mr. Swardt stating that he would soon leave Japan for China and is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 21st of this month.

Invitation to All Sectors to Discuss Assistance. Rice Merchants Across the Country Voluntarily Boycott. The result was a decision to voluntarily boycott. Of the 600,000 bags of Siamese rice previously ordered by Shanghai rice merchants from Hengfeng Rice Store, 385,000 bags have already been shipped to Shanghai, and the remaining 215,000 bags will be fully shipped to Shanghai and settled by the end of this month, after which no further orders will be placed.

Relief Plan for Displaced Overseas Chinese, Joint Review Meeting by Public Security, Social Affairs, and Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureaus 113

Mr. Jian Jinglun, Director of the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, once held a joint meeting with the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus regarding the relief of displaced overseas Chinese returning to the country and drafted a relief plan. Now, after Director Yin Guanzhi of the Public Security Bureau prepared a plan, it is scheduled to be decided at another joint meeting at the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau on the 18th of this month and implemented immediately. The proposed measures are as follows: (A) Relief Principles: 1. All displaced overseas Chinese forced to return to the country and arriving in Shanghai will be jointly responsible for relief by the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, Social Affairs Bureau, and Public Security Bureau. 2. Relief should be provided to those who are indeed forced to return to the country, lack the ability to live, and are at risk of becoming destitute. 3. Relief will be based on repatriation to their place of origin. In special circumstances, after verification, they may be sent to other areas to find friends and relatives and seek other livelihoods. 4. If it is found that overseas Chinese, although forced to return to the country, have the ability to return to their place of origin on their own, they will not be provided with relief, but if they request care, it will be handled at any time. (B) Relief Measures: 1. Whenever displaced overseas Chinese arrive, whether discovered or self-reported, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau must verify and register them and be responsible for assessing whether relief is necessary. 2. Once the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau has verified the displaced overseas Chinese, it will notify the Public Security Bureau of their address, order them to take care of them properly, and send a letter to the Social Affairs Bureau to be responsible for repatriation to their place of origin. However, if the hometown association of the displaced overseas Chinese declares that it has the ability to do so, it may send a letter to the hometown association to repatriate them. 3. If a large number of displaced overseas Chinese return to the country and the situation is very special, and the Social Affairs Bureau and the hometown association lack the ability to repatriate them, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau may submit a special request to the government for relief. 4. If there are displaced overseas Chinese who have fallen into depravity and are unwilling to return to their place of origin and are sufficient to affect public order, they may be forcibly repatriated. (C) Procedures: 1. Registration must record in detail from which country they were forced to return, the circumstances of their forced return, and their economic situation to facilitate investigation. 2. Assessment should be as realistic as possible, and notification should be simple and quick. 3. Repatriation and care should be as quick and efficient as possible to achieve results.

A Teenager Commits Suicide in Changhua Hotel 125

It was only until noon yesterday that the waiter called him to get up as usual, but there was no response from room No. 13.
