The Wife of a Tailor Dies Tragically, Scissors Stabbed into Her Abdomen, The Court Conducted an Examination of the Corpse Yesterday 126

Wang Cai, a woman from Shaoxing, was twenty-six years old. Her husband, Wang Zhengyu, was a tailor, and they lived together at No. 161 Dalianwan Road. At around 5:00 PM on the 11th of this month, she held a pair of scissors and walked up to the sleeping area on the second floor, intending to cut clothes. As soon as she reached the second floor, she suddenly fell to the ground due to carelessness, causing the scissors she was holding to accidentally stab her abdomen, about several points deep. Blood flowed like a river, and she cried out in pain. Her husband discovered the incident and tried to bandage her wound and helped her to bed. On the afternoon of the 13th, Wang saw that his wife's injuries were getting worse and took her to Guangren Hospital. The treatment was ineffective, and she died yesterday. The hospital reported the incident to the Yulin Road Police Station, and the investigators were ordered to investigate. The body was then taken to the corpse examination office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Tang, the prosecutor from the Shan First Special District Local Court, arrived at the office to examine the body, interrogated Wang Zhengyu, and learned about the previous situation. The coroner found that the deceased, Wang Cai, was a female and died after being stabbed by scissors before her death. The body was taken back for coffin burial after her husband, Wang Zhengyu, signed a guarantee.

Xin Ning Shao Collides with Chuanshan Ship, Chuanshan Damages Head and Right Cabin, Sailed That Day Back to Shanghai for Inspection 128

The Chuanshan ship of Chuanshan Shipping Company, weighing 1,029 tons, which traveled on the line of Dinghai Shipu and Haimen Chuanshan, left the Jinliyuan Xinjiangtian Wharf at 5:10 pm on the 15th. As soon as the ship left the wharf, the bow turned south and turned its head with the tide. Then the Ning Shao Si Boban ship Xin Shao (3,407 tons) also drove north from the No. 1 Wharf of Nanshi at this time, and the drum ship went down with the current, just in time for the bow of Chuanshan. It was too late to avoid it, causing a collision. The outer side of the iron plate and the angle iron of the right side of the bow of the Chuanshan ship and the small door, etc., were all damaged. The front cabin of the second calendar A was also found to be broken due to the violent collision. After the owner of Chuanshan invited the chief mate of the Xinning Shao ship to the Chuanshan ship to inspect the damaged parts and register them to prepare for negotiations, he reported to the Jianghai Customs and the company, and then each sailed out. The damage to Chuanshan was at the upper end of the ship's body, which did not hinder navigation. Chuanshan Company plans to wait until next Tuesday, when the Chuanshan ship returns to Shanghai, and then ask a notary to inspect the damage, estimate the loss, and demand compensation from Ning Shao Company. The document of Chuanshan Shipping Company's report to the Customs Maritime Administration and the insurance company yesterday is recorded as follows: This past Wednesday at 5:10 pm, the Chuanshan ship sailed from the Xinjiangtian Wharf, the ship's head was heading south, and the tide was falling. Chuanshan was just turning around with the tide, and the Xinning Shao ship of Ning Shao Company was also starting from Nanshi and going down with the current, causing a collision on the right side of the head cabin of the Chuanshan ship, and the iron plate angle iron small door, etc. were damaged in many places, and the two-story cabin was also damaged and cracked. The chief mate of Xinning Shao has already inspected the ship. Chuanshan immediately sailed out, and will ask the engineer to inspect it next Tuesday when it returns to Shanghai and formally negotiate compensation with Ning Shao Company.

Bathing Buddha Festival: Dispute over the Collection of Stall License Fees, Wang Dezhang and Others Organize a Stallholders' Association, the Police Believe it is Extortion and Arrest Wang for Prosecution 129

Superstitious people have traditionally regarded the eighth day of the fourth lunar month as the Bathing Buddha Festival. On this day, Jing'an Temple in western Shanghai holds a Buddhist ceremony, attracting a continuous stream of women devotees. Taking advantage of this opportunity, small vendors set up stalls near the temple to sell various goods, a practice that has been going on for a long time. Subsequently, the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which is in charge of the area, found that the number of stallholders increased year by year, setting up stalls along the roadside in a disorderly manner. Therefore, regulations were created for stallholders to obtain licenses, dividing the stall locations and setting up stalls according to the designated locations to avoid disputes. As for the license application procedures, stallholders had to go to Jing'an Temple in advance to

Register

Each stallholder paid a license fee of four yuan and sixty cents. The temple collected the names of all stallholders and submitted them to the Donation Office to apply for business licenses before setting up stalls for trade. The police station also dispatched special officers to the scene to protect them. Although these markets were held only for a short period of time, the transactions were very prosperous, so the number of stallholders increased year by year, reportedly reaching as many as 1,600 households. Those who obtained licenses earned more profits, which aroused the envy of Wang Dezhang. Wang is a member of the 34th branch of the Citizens' Association and resides in a cigarette and paper shop at No. 148 Hart Road. Before this year's

Bathing Buddha Festival

He gathered Feng Guangjia, Wu Youchun, and others to organize a so-called Jing'an Temple Incense Fair Stallholders' Association, with the sole purpose of applying for licenses on behalf of the incense fair stallholders. They notified the stallholders to register with the association first, paying a registration fee of one yuan per household. At the same time, they negotiated with the abbot of Jing'an Temple to transfer the license application business, but the temple was unwilling to let go of its vested interests and rejected the request. This matter was heard by the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which believed that they were fabricating a name to

Extort Money

So four days before the Bathing Buddha Festival, they arrested Wang and searched his home, finding seventeen books of printed receipts, as well as leaflets, seals, and other items. However, he denied recognizing Tang Zihong and Tan Yueguan Huchen. An investigation revealed that Wang had printed a total of twenty receipt books, but three books were missing, indicating that some stallholders had undoubtedly been deceived. The police lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, filed a public prosecution on charges of fraud. The First Special District Court submitted a proposal for inquiry and deliberated on releasing him on bail of nine hundred yuan to await further investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiang Yinghua conducted a further interrogation. Wang Wuzhang confessed that he had received ninety-five yuan in registration fees from the stallholders, but because of

Police Intervention

He had refunded seventy-nine yuan, leaving only sixteen yuan. He also claimed that the Incense Fair Stallholders' Association was initiated and organized with Feng and Wu, but it had not been officially established yet. The original site of the association, all the meeting minutes, and other documents were kept by the clerk Tu Qing. Because Wang has gone to Hangzhou, he was unable to submit them for inspection. According to the report, the police heard Wang's statement and immediately declared that it was probably not true, requesting that the bail be revoked and Wang be detained, and that all the books and documents be quickly transferred to the case to prevent the destruction of evidence. The judge deliberated and changed the defendant's bail to one thousand yuan, and immediately sent police to seize the books. The case was returned for further investigation.

Male and Female Workers Fight in Lihua Sock Factory, Mediator Dies Tragically, French Police Arrest Husband and Wife 130

Xu Zhenjiu, an Anhui native, 31 years old, lived with his wife at No. 128 Lafayette Road in the French Concession of this port. He worked at the Lihua Sock Factory at No. 35 Shoufu Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession. A new female worker, Zhu Liubao, entered the factory to learn the trade, and was taught by Su Desheng, an Anhui native. Su asked the female worker for two yuan for a treat, but the female worker did not have the money at the time, so she pawned a woolen shirt for one yuan and six jiao, still short of six jiao. It was agreed that she would pay the remaining amount when she received her salary. When salaries were paid a few days ago, Su Desheng asked the female worker for the money but failed to get it, and an argument broke out. The female worker went home and told her husband. On the 14th, at 12:00 noon, the female worker went to the factory with her husband, and Su Desheng questioned her. They then had a verbal conflict and began to pull and beat each other. Xu Zhenjiu stepped forward to mediate and was accidentally kicked in the lower abdomen, causing serious injury. He died at 6:00 AM yesterday. Lihua Company's Decorated Archway Accidentally Caught Fire Last Night, Did Not Extend to the Interior 131

The Lihua Department Store, located at the corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road, had a decorated archway in front of its main entrance advertising a large-scale sale of pine and cypress trees. Due to prolonged exposure to the sun and night dew, it was unusually dry. At around 7:00 PM last night, the electric lights on the archway, which spelled out "Large Sale," somehow caught fire, causing the fire to spread to the pine and cypress trees. In an instant, the flames soared. Although the company used its own firefighting equipment and made every effort to extinguish the fire, the wind was too strong, and it was like trying to put out a cartload of burning wood with a cup of water. At that time, the traffic on the road was in chaos, and neighboring businesses closed their doors one after another. Soon, someone reported to the Fire Brigade, which dispatched pump trucks to the scene. At the same time, the Electric Light Company cut off the power supply. The decorated archway and flags were completely destroyed. Fortunately, the wind was blowing from south to north, so the interior of Lihua was not affected. Only a portion of the goods, which were hit by the water hose, suffered slight water damage. Traffic on Nanjing Road was stopped for about half an hour.

Chen Yipeizhen Sues for the Return of Her Child 132

Husband and wife claim the child, Baobao, is theirs, each side sticks to their own story, mediation fails.

Chen Yipeizhen, a woman from Beiping residing at No. 2, Jiusi Lane, Bushi Road, French Concession, 31 years old, recently appointed lawyer Zhang Ding to file a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the Second Special District Court, requesting that Chen Zhou, a local woman currently residing at No. 260, Beile Road, 40 years old, be summoned for mediation and the return of her biological son. According to the petition, in 1923, she married Chen Yide, a businessman, as a concubine. Due to his Catholic beliefs, he could not take a concubine, so he rented No. 102, Yongfu Lane, Edouard Road, and lived with Chen for several years. On July 21, 1926, at 6:35 AM, Yipeizhen gave birth to a son, nicknamed Xiong Guan, academically named Nengyi. In May 1927, Yipeizhen became ill and could not raise the child, so she handed Xiong Guan over to Chen De, who died soon after. The family was embroiled in a property dispute, and the claimant's child was used to preserve the family property. Nengyi is now growing older, and the claimant misses her son dearly and intends to take him back for her own upbringing and education. Therefore, she filed a petition requesting mediation and that Nengyi be returned to the claimant for upbringing. The court granted the request and yesterday morning at 2:00 AM, Judge Li Yishu convened the seventh civil court to gather the two parties for mediation. Both parties were represented by lawyers. First, the claimant's lawyer stated the intention of the request for mediation and presented three photos of the claimant with Chen Yide and the child Nengyi. The opposing party's lawyer, representing Chen Zhou, completely denied the claimant's lawyer's claims, stating that although the photos presented by the claimant's side were taken with Chen Yide, they could not be used as conclusive evidence, because taking photos together does not prove a biological relationship. The claimant's lawyer further stated that the claimant's birth of Nengyi could be proven by an obstetrician. At this point, the court considered that the two parties' statements were contradictory and mediation was impossible. Therefore, they declared that mediation had failed and instructed the claimant to file a formal lawsuit separately. The court adjourned.

Informant Li Zhucheng Plants Red Pills to Take Revenge, Mastermind Li Kuifu Frames Someone, Fortunately, a Guard from the Airfield Testifies 133

On the morning of the first of this month, Geng Shoubao, the leader of the detective squad stationed at the Caojiadu Public Security Branch in western Shanghai, received a report from informant Li Zhucheng (34 years old, from Henan) stating that a Wang family in a bungalow near the Hongqiao Road airfield in western Shanghai had a large-scale organization selling red pill drugs, using trucks to secretly transport the red pills in fuel tanks, so their business was quite prosperous. If the report was false, he was willing to be punished according to the law. Squad leader Geng reported to Director Wang for approval, and in the evening, he led the entire detective team, along with the informant and patrol police, to the Hongqiao Road police station and went to the address pointed out by the informant. After searching the premises, they found nothing. The head of the household, Wang Bende, was a driver in the guard camp stationed at the airfield. He knew he had been framed and was explaining to Squad Leader Geng when the informant suddenly claimed to have found a package of red pills and showed it to everyone. At that time, the airfield guards who had heard the news rushed to the scene to testify that Wang's business was legitimate and confirmed that the informant was planting evidence to frame him. Wang Bende also stated that he had known the informant Li Zhucheng for a long time and had a grudge against him. They were all taken back to the Caojiadu Branch. According to Li's confession, the mastermind was Li Kuifu, who was currently working as a gatekeeper at a public school on Xinzha Road. Because he had a feud with Wang, he instructed Li to frame him. Personnel were dispatched to arrest Li Kuifu, but he could not be found. The case was then transferred to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. Before the other day, Squad Leader Geng led the detectives and secretly went to the school and arrested Li Kuifu. According to Li's confession, he was 45 years old, from Anhui, and worked as a gatekeeper at the public school on Xinzha Road. He had a wife and a son and a daughter. He, Wang Bende, and Li Zhucheng were all acquaintances. Because he had a deep feud with Wang, he instructed Li to plant evidence to frame him in order to get revenge. The reason was that Wang had invested 300 yuan in a car with the people last year, but he was swallowed and profited alone. Not only was the investment not returned, but he had also repeatedly sneaked into his house this year and seduced and slept with his wife. He was caught and severely rebuked to avoid publicity, but it was still ineffective, so he held a grudge in his heart and discussed a plan with Li Zhucheng. He instructed Li to prepare red pills and secretly hide them in Wang's fuel tank two days before going to Wang's house, and then sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau to report it. He reported to the bureau that it was true. Because the case involved planting evidence to frame someone with a grudge, a document was prepared yesterday and sent to the bureau for investigation.

Two Fingers Chopped Off, Qiu Yushi Seems to Have a Mental Illness, Yuan Laosan's Testimony Cannot Be Relied On 134

At around 8:00 PM the night before last, Qiu Yushi, a Shandong native residing at No. 478, Bei Hutang Road, Pudong, accompanied by witness Yuan Laosan, reported to the Machine Gun Team Headquarters of the Lujiazui Municipal Public Security Bureau that at around 6:00 PM that evening, the plaintiff went to the Taitongxin Rice Shop at No. 394, Bei Hutang Road, to buy 200 wen of rice. Because the shop assistant gave him too little rice, he reached out to grab a handful of rice. The shop assistant, Yang Hongkui, threatened to chop off his fingers. He was furious and asked if he had a knife. Yang then took out a kitchen knife, which he took and chopped off his left middle finger and ring finger himself. While speaking, he presented two fingers and requested an investigation. According to witness Yuan, he saw the shop assistant, Zhao Zhihui, holding a long knife and forcibly chopping off the plaintiff's two fingers. The team leader immediately sent police to take both defendants to the team and transferred them to the Pudong Branch. Director Zhang interrogated the plaintiff and witness separately, but their statements were different and contradictory. He then questioned the two defendants, who insisted that the plaintiff had not come to the shop to buy rice or have his fingers chopped off. Director Zhang found many suspicious points in the plaintiff's accusation and went to the shop to investigate. He saw that there were no knife marks or bloodstains on the counter or the ground. According to passersby, the plaintiff had a mental illness that came and went, and sometimes he would even cut his own ears with a knife, but fortunately, it was taken away. The director suspected that the witness was using the plaintiff's chopped-off fingers to defraud someone, so he transferred both parties to the General Bureau for investigation yesterday. However, when they arrived at Dongmen Road in Puxi, the witness Yuan Laosan ordered the plaintiff to insist that the defendant Zhao Zhihui was the one who committed the crime. This was overheard by the escorting police, who reported it to Director Zhang, who was even more convinced that the witness was deliberately making trouble. Therefore, he prepared a second document reporting the mid-way instigation to the bureau for review.

This was followed by a piano performance by Ms. Hu Wenjie, a student at the Chinese and Western Girls' Middle School. Among the distinguished guests were Dr. Fraulein of the School for the Blind, Dr. Yan Fuqing, the president of the Red Cross Hospital, Dr. Niu Huisheng, the president of the Orthopedic Hospital representing Mrs. Niu Huisheng, Dr. Shi of the Bethel Hospital, and Dr. Ma of the Tongren Hospital, who gave congratulatory speeches. After that, Ms. Zhang Meiqing and Ms. Sun Yuanzhen, students at the Chinese and Western Girls' Middle School, sang, followed by a prayer by Pastor Yu Zhihan. Tea and refreshments were then served, and photos were taken before the meeting adjourned, which was a grand occasion. Zhou Zhenlin, Wang Binyan, Chen Yingfu, Jin Juefei, and others in the national goods industry in this city, in view of the huge trade deficit and rural bankruptcy in recent years, and in order to promote national goods and save the country from danger, have jointly initiated the organization of the Shanghai National Goods Market. Japanese Female Thief Nakamura Sueko Rampages in the South Sea 141

According to the Japanese-language Shanghai Daily, Nakamura Sueko, a beautiful Japanese woman who was once the wife of a pirate in the South Sea, has been based in Fuqing County, Fujian Province, since May of last year. She is a huge pirate who emerges at sea to rob passing ships for a living. Since falling in love with Chen Bailin, a Taiwanese, she has been admired by the bandits and has led her gang to rampage at sea. Later, she won Chen's favor, and all the items robbed from the ships were distributed at her discretion. In the autumn of last year, she suddenly missed her hometown, so she obtained 35,000 yuan in cash from the bandit leader and returned to Japan alone. Passing through Hong Kong and Taiwan, she secretly returned to her hometown of Hokkaido. Unexpectedly, after returning to her hometown, she was strongly denounced by the villagers and could not find a place to live. She had no choice but to return to Fujian and resume her life as a thief. However, at this time, the bandit leader had been killed by the army, and his gang had fled east and west, leaving only three or four confidants. Moreover, the Fujian provincial authorities were investigating very strictly, so she sneaked into the dark streets of Xiamen. When the bandits heard that Sueko had arrived, they gathered the remnants of the gang and planned to make a comeback. It is reported that a powerful naval team has now been formed, with her as the pirate king, engaged in robbery.

Xu Jinqing's Illegally Possessing Firearms Case Concluded; Xu Presents Gong Guoliang's Warrant as Evidence; Request for Bail Denied, Sentencing Scheduled 144

Xu Jinqing, former judicial police chief of the Shanghai Local Court, was previously prosecuted by Prosecutor Lei Binzhang for illegally possessing a handgun. As Xu repeatedly failed to appear in court, the case remained unresolved. Recently, Xu Jinqing, after returning to Shanghai from Zhenjiang, hired lawyer Sha Xunyi to file a petition requesting an expedited hearing. The court, acting on the petition, dispatched Police Chief Zhang Shuping on the 1st of this month at 4 PM to summon and detain Xu pending further investigation. Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, the newly appointed Criminal Court President Cai Dincheng presided over the hearing in the Third Tribunal. The defendant Xu Jinqing was defended by lawyers Sha Xunyi, Jin Yu, and Chen Heting, who appeared in court on his behalf. The judge ordered the detained Xu Jinqing to be brought before the court.

(Question): Age 42, from Wuxi, residing at No. 50 Taian Street, outside the West Gate. (Question): Have you ever committed a crime before? (Answer): No. (Question): Do you have any property, how do you live usually? (Answer): I still have land and businesses in my hometown. (Question): Have you received any education? (Answer): I studied at home since childhood. (Question): Who is in your family? (Answer): My father is deceased, my mother is alive, and I have a wife, a son, and a daughter. I also have brothers in my hometown. (Question): Regarding the handgun seized by the prosecutor at your home on July 8th, 1934, where did it come from? (Answer): It belonged to Gong Guoliang, the district chief of the 4th District of the Zhenjiang Water Police. Gong ordered his orderly Chen Xiangtao to send the gun to my house, instructing me to apply for a gun license on his behalf, with only a warrant from him. (This warrant had already been submitted as evidence.) Because at that time, there was no

official letter or Gong's photo, the procedures were not complete, so I didn't apply for the license yet. I kept the gun in my house to hold it for him. After I received the photo, I would then apply for the license. (Question): When was this gun given to you? (Answer): July 2nd of last year. The warrant and the gun were given to me at the same time, but the date on the warrant was June 30th. (Question): From July 2nd to July 8th, were you at home all the time? (Answer): I waited for three days, and when I didn't see any official letter sent, I left Shanghai on the 6th and went to Zhenjiang 4th District to serve. I was appointed by the Shanxi Police District Chief as a

district consultant. (Question): How many families live in your house? (Answer): Two families. One is the Wang Shuifang family. The Wang family lives downstairs and runs an insurance company. (Question): When the prosecutor searched your house, you asked him to leave, and the Wang family said you went to Hardoon Garden to have fun. (Answer): They were just guessing. I had already left Shanghai. (Question): According to you, someone sent you the gun on June 30th and asked you to get a license. Why hadn't you applied for the license by July 8th when the prosecutor searched your house, which was eight or nine days later? Besides, since it was Gong's gun, your wife should have known. Why didn't she say anything when the prosecutor raised the issue? (Answer): A photo was needed to apply for the license. Because no photo was sent, it was delayed. My wife did

explain to the prosecutor. I am indeed a consultant for the 4th District, and I have an appointment letter to prove it. (Question): When were you appointed? (Answer): I can't remember the date. (Question): Have you ever served in the Zhenjiang District? (Answer): I often resided in the district to serve. Besides, I once led a team to suppress bandits in Taihu Lake. When Gu Zhutong was the chairman of Jiangsu Province, I was the director of the investigation department of the Civil Affairs Department. That's why I haven't been back for a long time. (Question): Since the discovery of the handgun, it's been almost October. Why have you repeatedly failed to appear when summoned? (Answer): Although I sometimes went to Shanghai, because I didn't ask for leave and left overnight, I didn't report to the case. Although District Chief Gong has resigned, I still served in the district after the successor District Chief Wang took over. After I came to Shanghai, I

submitted a petition stating my request to be brought to trial. Because I only requested two weeks of leave. The judge said, "You should have reported earlier, and the case could have been concluded earlier, so you wouldn't have been delayed." (Answer): "I didn't know that your court had repeatedly summoned me. Now I ask the judge to forgive me. If I had lied, how would I dare to submit a petition myself?" (Question): Does District Chief Gong have another office in Shanghai? (Answer): No. Gong's district is the Zhenjiang 4th District. According to Jiangsu Province, there are four major districts. The first district is located in Minhang, Shanghai. The second district is located in Suzhou. The third district is located in Tongzhou. All are appointed by the Civil Affairs Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government.

At this point, Prosecutor Lei Binzhang came to court and argued that the defendant Xu Jinqing was illegally possessing a handgun. When searched, two gun licenses were found, but the numbers filled in did not match the number on the gun at all. During the investigation, the defendant repeatedly failed to appear, claiming that the handgun was entrusted by District Chief Gong to apply for a license on his behalf. If it was for applying for a license, why were there also three bullets? There was also no official document from the district chief to prove it. Furthermore, this handgun was found in the drawer in front of the bed, which proves that it belongs to the defendant. He should be publicly sentenced according to law. Xu Jinqing said that Gong's warrant was in his briefcase and was not handed over at the time, so there was a misunderstanding. Judge Cai then began the debate. Lawyer Sha Xunyi began by saying that Article 2 of the Regulations on Military Firearms and Artillery stipulates that anyone who possesses firearms and cannot prove that there is a legitimate reason for doing so

constitutes a punishable offense. Conversely, if a person possesses firearms and can prove that there is a legitimate reason for doing so, it is not restricted by the regulations. The meaning is very clear. The legislative intention is not to restrict the people's ability to possess firearms, but to prevent the people from abusing them and affecting public order. In this case, the defendant's reason for possessing the handgun was that he was entrusted by District Chief Gong of the Water Police to apply for a concession license. Furthermore, it was found during the search in a locked drawer and was not placed outside, so there was no possibility of using it at any time.

Due to the nature of his duties and with the written proof from District Chief Gong of the Water Police, it is indeed a fact, and there is obviously no situation where he cannot prove that there is a legitimate reason. It does not seem to fall within the scope of a crime under the legislative intent of Article 2 of the Regulations on Military Firearms and Artillery. According to law, there is no possibility of constituting a crime. He requested that Xu Jinqing be declared innocent. Then, lawyers Jin Yu and Chen Heting stood up one after another to defend him for a long time. The general meaning was the same as what Lawyer Sha said. He requested bail in court. Judge Cai stated that the case was clear, and then announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the 20th of this month. The request for bail was difficult to approve. He then ordered that the prisoner be taken back into custody pending instructions. By the time court adjourned, the bell had rung five times.

Unfilial Son Injures His Elderly Father 149

Guang Annian, a local resident of No. 19 Chunjiang Lane, Chunjiang Road, Pudong, is in his sixties and has a son named Fugen, who is 28 years old. He has always been well-behaved. Recently, he met a woman outside and wanted to move out and live separately. At 6 PM the day before yesterday, Fugen was diligently carrying things. His father asked where he was moving to and how he could bear to leave his elderly father alone. Fugen replied that he was moving to Jiangsu Province. His father was so angry that he grabbed his son and refused to let him go. Unexpectedly, Fugen became angry and used a long bench to hit his father's left eye, creating a hole between his temples. Blood flowed all over his face, and he fell to the ground. The police took the father and son to the Pudong Branch for questioning. The bureau first sent the injured person to the Pudong Hospital for treatment and then waited for the interrogation.

New Compilation Catalog of the Authors' Bookstore 150

The Authors' Bookstore was founded in October 1922 and is one of the emerging bookstores. The founder, Mr. Huang Buxiang, served in the Commercial Press for nearly twenty years. After the January 28th Incident, the Authors' Bookstore was established at Nos. 271-273 Fuzhou Road. "To do our best for authors and serve readers" is its only belief and wish. The bookstore has accepted more than 6,000 kinds of books for consignment sales. It has opened a new era of division of labor between publishing and distribution. It was registered with the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of the Ministry of Industry in January 1935 and obtained a certificate. The bookstore has recently compiled and distributed catalogs to all sectors in response to the needs of more than 100,000 readers and to facilitate the selection of libraries. The catalog is bound in a unique way, using a loose-leaf format, so that it can be assembled and disassembled freely. The bookstore compiled this catalog with great sacrifice and decided to follow the Cumulative Book Index method published by the American W.H. Wilson Co. In the future, single-page national publication catalogs will be compiled and distributed monthly. Those who have this catalog can disassemble and assemble it in this catalog for replenishment at any time. Over the years, it will become a complete general catalog of national publications. In the future, readers can avoid the tediousness of requesting catalogs from various bookstores. Improving culture and introducing academics are great achievements, and facilitating readers is only a trivial matter. Anyone who needs it only needs to attach three cents of postage to receive it. It is said that within a week of publication, more than 100,000 copies have been distributed.

Tangshan Jiaotong University 30th Anniversary; Shanghai Tangshan Alumni Gather for a Celebration Dinner 153

The 15th of this month was the 30th anniversary of the founding of Tangshan Jiaotong University. Tangshan alumni in Shanghai held a meeting at the Atlantic Western Restaurant on 4th Road to celebrate. Dozens of people attended, making it very lively. At 7 PM, everyone took their seats. First, Chairman Huang Airu reported on the history of the alma mater and the contributions of past alumni to Chinese engineering. Then, he reported on the recent development of the alma mater and the plans for the future. Finally, he reported on the preparations for the celebration of the alma mater and alumni associations in various places, and said that this celebration is not only to encourage the spirit of alumni to protect the school, but also to promote social attention to this engineering school with a glorious history, and hope that the Chinese people will catch up quickly to consolidate this national defense front. Next, Zhang Xiaoji, the captain of the Shanghai Fundraising Team of the Architectural Alumni Association, reported on the results of the fundraising of the alumni in Shanghai and the process of sending representatives to Tangshan to participate in the school's annual meeting and the groundbreaking ceremony of the alumni association. Then, Qiu Qihua, an old alumnus of the school, gave a speech on the meaning and necessity of the alumni association and how to promote its development. Alumnus Fang Huanru reported on the current situation of engineering construction in emerging countries and the treatment of engineers, and encouraged all alumni to respect themselves and start from hard work, not forgetting the Tangshan character. In the future, when the national construction is completed and the material civilization is developed, food, clothing, housing, and transportation will be sufficient, then the social habit of underestimating engineers will eventually be broken, and they will sing the praises of the lofty greatness of the engineering commander. Then, the chairman offered a speech, and the whole group stood up, raised their glasses to wish the alma mater a long life, cheered, and then the meeting ended. Chairman Huang talked about the brief history of Tangshan Jiaotong University as follows: Tangshan Jiaotong University was originally transformed from the Shanhaiguan Official School. If calculated from the Shanhaiguan Official School, it will have been 40 years by now. It is the earliest engineering and material specialty school in China. The Shanhaiguan Official School was destroyed by fire during the Boxer Rebellion. Therefore, in the 31st year of Guangxu, the old professors were summoned to build Tangshan Jiaotong University in Tangshan. At first, it was named Tangshan Road and Mining School. The first class graduated in 1912. At that time, 23 people took the exam to become engineers for the Yuehan Road project, and all of them were admitted. (A total of 28 people were admitted, and their reputation spread throughout the national engineering community, thus opening up the reputation of Tangshan for hard work in the engineering community. Later, it was changed to Tangshan Industrial Vocational School. In 1917, the Ministry of Education investigated the performance of vocational schools across the country, and Tangshan was especially known for its first-place performance in the country. Later, a mechanical engineering department was added. Later, it was combined with Nanyang and Beijing schools to form Jiaotong University. Later, the three schools were separated, and Tangshan was called Tangda. After that, it was merged. Tangshan is now called Jiaotong University Tangshan Engineering School. Now a mining department has been added, which is becoming more and more perfect. It is indeed the engineering school with the longest history and the best results in China's construction.

Weather Report 160

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, stating that the Shandong area is cloudy but still fine, with an indefinite wind direction, due to a low pressure in Mongolia moving eastward. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and unstable, with a possibility of rain, and winds ranging from southeast to northeast, due to a small low pressure moving eastward. The East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait are overcast, with a sharp northeast wind. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai within 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 77.4 degrees, and the lowest was 54.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 80.6 degrees, and the lowest was 59.4 degrees.

Letter to the Editor 161

To the Editor: I have just read a news item in the "Local Correspondences" column of your newspaper on the 15th regarding a lawsuit against Kunshan County Magistrate Peng, which does not conform to the facts. After investigation, in the case of Wang Chengjia and Wei Rongting from this county last July, suspected of fraud, Wang Pijia has long failed to appear in court. The county government, in accordance with judicial procedures, presented it to the High Court for approval of an arrest warrant. Subsequently, Wang Pijia petitioned the High Court to transfer jurisdiction of the case, but it was not approved. Wang then appealed to the Supreme Court, which ordered the High Court to re-adjudicate. Now, the High Court has approved the transfer of the entire file to the Wuxian District Court for trial, so that Wang Pijia and Wei Rongting can confront each other. Recently, a ruling was issued ordering the county government to send a police officer to deliver it to Pijia. As for what was stated that County Magistrate Peng had received a summons and gone to Suzhou to await questioning, this is not the case. Please correct this. Thank you very much. Addressed to: Editorial Department of Shen Bao Newspaper, Kunshan County Government, May 16th.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Summons Principals in Yunnan, Giving Instructions: The Essence of the New Life Movement to Discipline Students 163

(Central News Agency, Kunming, 16th) On the 15th, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek summoned principals and military training directors of secondary schools and above at the headquarters to give instructions. The key points were: (1) Universities and specialized schools should focus on improving quality, and the Sino-French Gengkuan funds will be used to subsidize Yunnan University. (2) The people of Yunnan are simple and honest. It is hoped that all schools will strictly discipline and train students according to the essence of the New Life Movement. Special attention should be paid to the organization and management of affairs to cultivate their strong administrative abilities. The purpose of education is threefold: to make the best use of people's talents, to make the best use of the land, and to make the best use of resources. To achieve these three goals, one must start by improving students' moral knowledge and physical fitness, that is, by implementing the New Life Movement as a foundation. If students are well-trained at school, they will surely influence others, and when they go to society, they will be able to influence society. Like the wind bending the grass, the effects will be great. (3) Military training is the foundation for teaching students how to be people, to cultivate them into citizens with the five virtues of wisdom, trust, benevolence, courage, and strictness, that is, to cultivate their lives to be militarized. It is hoped that this spirit will be used to intensify training.

Secondary School Normal Education Research Association: Second Plenary Meeting Held Yesterday 167

Director Pan Presides, Each Group Reports on Research Results, Members Elected to Review and Decide, Meeting Continues This Afternoon

The Secondary School Normal Education Research Association of this city held its second plenary meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday on the ninth floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. Director Pan presided. The meeting will continue this afternoon at 4:00 PM. The details are as follows:

Attendees: Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Section Chief Zeng Shengdian, Specialist Zhou Shang, Qian Jinggong, and others; experts and members Tai Shuangqiu, Zheng Xigu, Liao Maoru; members from Minli, Nanyang, Chengzhong, Lida, Xinlu, Wuben, Jingye, Guanghua, Daxia, McLun, Zhongzhi, Dazhong, Private Shanghai, Youshi, Minguang, Shanghai Women's, Huadong, Aiqun, Daozhong, Yangjing, Peiming, Dongfang, Minzhi, Kunfan, Minli Girls' High School, Guangdong East, Huzhou, South Model, and other schools, totaling over fifty principals.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Pan, Director of the Bureau, rose and reported, briefly stating that the Secondary School Normal Education Research Association, based on the research questions issued by the Ministry of Education, held its second plenary meeting today. Since the first meeting, five groups were formed to research the questions issued by the Ministry separately. Now, each group has completed its research and presented it to this meeting for further discussion. It was originally scheduled for the 15th, but because I and many principals went to Suzhou to attend the supplementary ceremony for the fourth military training team, it was scheduled for today. The agenda of this meeting is as follows: First, the chairman of each group will report on the research results separately, and then experts and members Tai Shuangqiu, Zheng Xigu, and Liao Maoru will express their opinions. After exchanging discussions, a general review will be conducted to obtain conclusions, which will be reported to the Ministry of Education by the Education Bureau for reference, and so on.

Group Reports: (A) Liao Maoru reported the research opinions of the curriculum teaching group: (1) The Ministry of Education is requested to stipulate the minimum curriculum timetable for each subject in senior and junior high schools, which local schools can use as the most flexible adaptation based on special circumstances; (2) Revise the current timetable based on the actual problems raised by the Ministry of Education. (B) Chen Jicheng reported the research opinions of the graduation joint examination group: (1) School graduation examinations should be abolished; (2) The academic status of high school students who fail one or two subjects after two supplementary examinations but have been admitted to a junior college or above for a probationary period is considered to be recognized without supplementary examinations if the probationary results are good; (3) Normal school students who fail one or two subjects in the excellent graduation joint examination should be allowed to serve first, but should not be allowed to teach the failed subjects; (4) The calculation and disclosure methods of the school's joint examination results standards; (5) Request the Ministry of Education to issue a notice to all public and private universities in the country that all entrance examination questions for new students should be in Chinese and should be based on the curriculum standards issued by the Ministry to facilitate students' further education. (C) Ni Wenya reported the research opinions of the funding equipment group: (1) Seven methods for establishing natural sciences in secondary and normal schools; (2) Two opinions on equipment standards; (3) Opinions on the Ministry's funding allocation standards; (4) Opinions on how to reform the malpractices of ticket forgery and shops. (D) Sheng Zhensheng reported the research opinions of the teacher training group. (E) Tang Zenghong reported the opinions of the moral and military training group.

Expert Opinions: After the chairman of each group reported, expert members expressed their opinions. Zheng Xigu, Liao Maoru, He Shuangqiu, and others expressed many supplementary opinions on teacher training, curriculum teaching, equipment funding, graduation joint examinations, and other issues. Finally, Tai Shuangqiu, Zheng Xigu, Liao Maoru, Sheng Zhensheng, Jia Foru, Ni Wenya, and Shen Tongyi were appointed to jointly review the opinions of each group and submit a written opinion. The meeting will continue today to discuss it.

Continuing Meeting Today: The plenary meeting will continue to be held on the ninth floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at 4:00 PM today to discuss the written opinion. At 7:00 PM in the evening, Pan, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, will host a banquet for all members at the original location. Invitations have already been sent out yesterday.

Municipal Education and Health Bureaus Pay Attention to Children's Health Activities During Holidays: Preparing to Organize the Children's Holiday Health Activities Promotion Association - Regulations Have Been Announced, and Preparations for Establishment Are Underway 170

The Municipal Health and Education Bureaus, in order to announce the regulations of the Shanghai Children's Holiday Health Activities Promotion Association, jointly issued a public notice yesterday, stating that the health of children's bodies and minds depends on appropriate care. Governments of various countries and civil groups often use holidays to hold various children's health activities, and want to use the opportunity of children's summer vacations to give them opportunities to exercise their bodies and minds. The bureau, etc., in view of this, have also initiated and promoted such activities, such as last year's Children's Summer Health Camp, which is one example. Although the matter is an innovation, the results are not without promise. However, because the responsibility is heavy and the affairs are cumbersome, it is difficult to achieve greater progress without gathering the strength of the entire society. In terms of economic talent, it is also beyond the ability of the bureau, etc., to take on alone. Therefore, it is planned to organize the Shanghai Children's Holiday Health Activities Promotion Association, inviting relevant agencies, groups, and manufacturers to join, to be a permanent group responsible for the city's children's holiday health activities. All regulations have been formulated. In addition to submitting them to the municipal government for record and starting preparations for establishment, it is necessary to publicize them for all to know. Agencies, groups, and manufacturers who are enthusiastic about promoting children's health activities are expected to freely register with the Education Bureau for participation before May 20 to facilitate recruitment. Special notice is hereby given. The regulations of the Shanghai Children's Holiday Health Activities Promotion Association are attached as follows:

(1) The Education Bureau and the Health Bureau are establishing the Shanghai Children's Holiday Health Promotion Association (hereinafter referred to as the Association) to implement health education and improve children's physical and mental health during holidays. (2) The tasks of the Association are as follows: (1) Donate funds; (2) Transfer personnel; (3) Send advertisements for publication; (4) Write and provide opinions; (5) Recommend experts for voluntary guidance; (6) Other matters related to children's health activities during holidays. (3) In addition to the Directors of the Education Bureau and the Health Bureau serving as ex officio members of the Association, the following personnel will also be appointed by the two bureaus to form the Association: (1) Health Education Specialist of the Education Bureau; (2) School Health Technician of the Health Bureau; (3) Medical experts in various fields and medical research groups; (4) Representatives of cultural institutions, Western medicine companies, charitable organizations, and children's health-related businesses. (4) The Association shall have three standing committee members, and one person shall be the standing chairman, all of whom shall be elected by the Association. (5) The Association shall have one secretary to be responsible for recording, communication, and other matters, who shall be appointed concurrently by the Director of the Education Bureau from among the staff of the Education Bureau. (6) The Association shall not hold regular meetings, but shall be convened by the Education Bureau and the Health Bureau when necessary. (7) The Mayor may be invited to attend meetings of the Association for guidance. (8) Important matters discussed at meetings of the Association must be submitted to the Education Bureau and the Health Bureau for approval before implementation. (9) These regulations may be submitted for amendment at any time if there are any deficiencies. (10) These regulations shall come into effect from the date of joint promulgation by the Education Bureau and the Health Bureau.

Qingdao Summer Training Camp: Qualifications for Participation 174

The regulations of the China National Sports Advancement Association's summer training camp are published as follows:

(1) This Association is organizing the summer training camp to prepare for participation in the World Games and to improve our country's sports performance and spirit.

(2) This training camp will be held at National Shandong University in Qingdao.

(3) The training items of this training camp are specified as follows: 1. Men's track and field; 2. Men's swimming; 3. Men's basketball.

(4) This training camp will be held from July 10th to August 20th.

(5) Athletes participating in this training camp must possess one of the following qualifications: (1) Track and field and swimming: (A) National record holders officially announced by this Association this year; (B) Those who have broken national records after the 1933 National Games and have proof from a formal sports organization; (C) Those who meet the following performance standards:

Track and Field Standards

100 meters: 11 seconds

200 meters: 23 seconds

400 meters: 53.1 seconds

800 meters: 2 minutes 5 seconds

1500 meters: 4 minutes 21.4 seconds

10,000 meters: 34 minutes 1 second

High hurdles: 16.6 seconds

Intermediate hurdles: 59 seconds

High jump: 1.80 meters

Long jump: 6.80 meters

Triple jump: 14 meters

Pole vault: 3.60 meters

Javelin: 50 meters

Discus: 37 meters

16-pound shot put: 12.50 meters

Swimming standards to be determined. (2) Basketball: A. Twelve to fifteen people selected by the selection committee hired by this Association (attached selection principles): A selection committee of three members will be established. Each member will propose potential athletes, noting each athlete's experience and achievements. Then, the athletes proposed by the three members will be gathered together, and each member will recommend eighteen people. From the athletes recommended by the two members, the chairman will decide the number of people who should be selected. B. In addition to those selected above, each sports organization may select and send excellent athletes to participate in the training camp. Those who pass the examination will be admitted.

(6) The regulations for travel and accommodation expenses for participants in this training camp are as follows: 1. Those participating with the qualifications in item (A) of the above clause (1) and (2) will have their travel and accommodation expenses covered by this Association and will receive a food allowance of 10 yuan. 2. Those participating with the qualifications in items (B) and (C) of the above clause (1) will bear all expenses themselves, but if they can break the standards set in the above clause during the training period, their travel expenses will be reimbursed by this Association. 3. Those participating with the qualifications in item (B) of the above clause (2) will have all expenses borne by the sending organization. (4) All athletes participating in this training camp must pay a food fee of 15 yuan (six weeks). Accommodation is free of charge.

(7) To participate in this training camp, regardless of qualifications, registration procedures must be completed. Participation is only allowed after passing the examination and receiving notification.

(8) The registration period for this training camp is from June 10th to June 25th. All applicants must send their applications directly to the Preparatory Office of this training camp at Shandong University in Qingdao by express mail.

(9) This training camp will have one director who will manage all matters of the training camp.

(10) This training camp will have one head coach, several coaches, and several assistant coaches to manage various training matters.

(11) The various training and management rules of this training camp will be determined separately.

(12) The organizational regulations of this training camp will be implemented after being passed by this Association.

Mr. Weilitun, the French Minister to China, has presented a silver cup to the Tennis Department of Aurora University, which will be used as a singles championship for alumni and students of the school. Those who have joined successively include Aurora, Jiaotong, St. John's, Shanghai, Datong, and Fudan, six universities. Yesterday, the captains of the six schools met and decided to start the competition this Sunday. The cup will be awarded based on the performance of each school. The league rules and competition order are listed below: (1) Name: Shanghai Universities' Weilitun Cup Tennis League; (2) Qualifications: Shanghai universities (invited to participate by Aurora University); (3) Player qualifications: Limited to current university students (middle school students can also represent their participating universities this year as an exception); (4) Number of matches: Twice a week (postponed in case of rain); (5) Competition date and time: Determined by the two schools in the competition, but limited to within one week of the draw; (6) Competition system: (A. Single round robin system; (B) Three singles and two doubles; (C) Best of three sets (7) Balls: Slazenger; (8) Player order: The order of singles and doubles players is based on the player list order written by each school in advance, or the order of the first match. If there is an absence, the singles players will move up in order and cannot move down. If one person is absent in doubles, a reserve player can replace them. If both players in the first group are absent, the second group will move up; (9) Location: Determined by drawing lots (can also be changed if both parties agree).

Page 14

Free Talk

The Mutual Influence of Literature Among Countries 186

— Wang Ji Cong

In the process of literary development, especially in modern literature, we can often see the mutual influence of literature among countries. What is the reason for this? We believe that the emergence or transplantation of a certain type of literature into a certain society is due to the certain needs of that society. If the literature of countries A and B have mutual influence in some areas, it also occurs under certain similar or identical social needs. However, the existence of similar social needs between countries A and B also has its actual basis; this basis lies in the fact that their social relationships have some kind of similarity. Only with this kind of similar social relationship can similar needs arise, and thus mutual influence can occur in literature as well. The so-called mutual influence of national literature does not occur unconditionally or without basis. George once said: "The influence of one country's literature on another is directly proportional to the similarity of the social relations between the two countries. Without this similarity, influence will not occur at all." In fact, although Europeans have long arrived in Africa, African blacks have not yet been influenced by European literature. The nomadic people in the Locke area at the junction of Sichuan, Gansu, Qinghai, and Kangding, although we have known about them for a long time, have not yet received the influence of our literature. Terms like Romanticism, Realism, and Neo-Realism are meaningless to their nomadic lives. ...These facts fully demonstrate that if there are no similar social relations, even if two countries or two kinds of people have communication, mutual influence in literature will not occur.

In the late 18th and early 19th centuries, for fifty or sixty years, the literary trend of Romanticism swept across Europe. Generally speaking, this literary trend first prevailed in England, and then blossomed in Germany and France. But in the entire Romantic movement, the three countries—England, Germany, and France—did have mutual influence. Although the surge of Romanticism in France occurred after England and Germany, Rousseau's advocacy of "returning to nature" had already laid a theoretical foundation for the entire Romantic movement. The successful performance of Hugo's "Hernani" not only demonstrated the victory of French Romanticism over Classicism, but also demonstrated the victory of Romanticism in Europe, and its influence spread throughout Europe. Similarly, Goethe in Germany and the so-called "Sturm und Drang" movement in Germany also had a great influence on the literature of England and France at that time. From this we can say that in the great tide of Romanticism, the literature of England, Germany, and France did have mutual influence. Needless to say, the occurrence of this mutual influence was also due to the similarity of social relations in England, Germany, and France. First of all, in the second half of the 18th century, England gradually embarked on an industrial capitalist society, and then Germany and France also transformed into countries with such social forms. The new emerging citizens, the masters of this industrial capitalist society, in order to pave the way for building their own literature, had to break the existing literary rules and negate Classicism. Thus, in the three countries—England, Germany, and France—which successively embarked on the road of industrial capitalist society, the literary trend of Romanticism occurred one after another. However, because the emerging industrial citizens were still young at that time and did not yet fully have the ability to dominate the new society, and even more lacked sufficient experience and cultivation in literature, they could not clearly express their independent social consciousness in literature. At the same time, the aristocracy was already declining, and of course did not have a positive upward consciousness, and even less could they express their dominating spirit in literature. Therefore, the Romanticism that appeared at this time, whether in England, Germany, or France, showed both aristocratic and mixed forms. This is clear evidence that the social relations of England, Germany, and France at that time had many similarities. Due to this similarity, the literature of England, Germany, and France had mutual influence at that time, and a surge of Romanticism occurred in their societies. Although the Romanticism that appeared in England, Germany, and France at that time also had its own differences, generally speaking, they were similar. The actual root of this similarity, of course, exists in their similar social relations.

If we shift the issue to China, it becomes even clearer. As everyone knows, since the imperialists used cannons to bombard open the flourishing gates of China in 1840, especially after the May Fourth New Culture Movement, the influence of Western European literature on Chinese literature has become an undeniable fact. Ibsen's individualism was greatly praised in China during the May Fourth era. The literary trends of Romanticism and Naturalism also exchanged in China after the 1990s. Subsequently, trends like Neo-Realism and Neo-Romanticism were also brought to China. In just a few decades, backward China almost transplanted all the literary phenomena that had gone through centuries in Europe. As a result, those nativists felt very uneasy, believing that Chinese literature following foreign literature was entirely created by a dozen or so writers who loved "foreign goods" and novelty. In order to preserve the national essence, they desperately opposed the influence of foreign literature on Chinese literature. In fact, the influence of Western European and even Japanese literature on Chinese literature was not created out of thin air by a small number of people who loved "foreign goods" and novelty, but was due to the many similarities between Chinese social relations and those of Western Europe and even Japan. Only when there was the existence of a bourgeoisie in China could bourgeois literature from Western Europe and Japan be transmitted to China; otherwise, even if Westerners and Japanese people entered the Chinese mainland, their bourgeois literature would not be accepted by China. Taking the May Fourth Literary Revolution as an example, many literary researchers believe that this revolution occurred entirely under the influence of foreign literature; even those who are more progressive regard the influence of foreign literature as one of the main reasons for the occurrence of the literary revolution. It is true that the May Fourth Literary Revolution was indeed greatly influenced by foreign literature, but this influence was not the fundamental reason for the revolution. On the contrary, it was because Chinese society had developed to the May Fourth era that it became necessary and possible to have such a literary revolution. On this necessity and possibility, on the needs of that kind of literary revolution, Western European literature then gave a strong influence to Chinese literature. More specifically, it was that Chinese social relations at that time had similarities with Western European social relations. Under the internal needs of Chinese society, Western European literature then influenced Chinese literature and caused the May Fourth Literary Revolution. Without this similarity, Western European literature would not have given such a great influence to Chinese literature, and thus it would not have had much to do with the Chinese Literary Revolution. Mr. Zhou Zuoren once made a clever explanation of the issue of Western European literature influencing the May Fourth Literary Revolution in his "The Origin and Development of New Chinese Literature": "Everything is ready, only the east wind is lacking"; then he said that the "east wind" here should be changed to "west wind." This means that the occurrence of the May Fourth Literary Revolution was because Chinese society had already possessed the conditions for the occurrence of this revolution, so it followed Western European society and accepted its literary trends, triggering a literary revolution. The so-called influence of Western European literature on Chinese literature at that time was not the fundamental reason for the occurrence of the May Fourth Literary Revolution, but only an external driving force of that revolution. Moreover, this driving force was attracted by the internal needs of Chinese society, due to the similarity between the social relations of China at that time and those of Western Europe.

So, why did Chinese literature in the May Fourth era not influence Western European literature, but only be influenced by Western European literature? Our answer is: Chinese society and culture were more backward than those of Western Europe. Modern society and its culture occurred latest in China. All the literary phenomena produced by Chinese society were not worth taking by the advanced Western European countries. On the contrary, the existing literature of the advanced Western European countries was urgently needed by backward China. Therefore, although Chinese social relations in the May Fourth era had some similarities with those of Western Europe, in fact, only Chinese literature followed Western European literature, only Chinese literature was influenced by Western European literature, and Chinese literature did not influence Western European literature.

From the above practical investigation, it can be seen that the issue of mutual influence of literature among countries occurs under similar social relations. At the same time, in countries with somewhat similar social relations, if one is more backward and the other is more advanced, then the literary influence is one-sided: that is, the more advanced influences the more backward. Currently, many people in China often angrily say: Chinese literature only follows Japan, and Japanese literature only follows Western European countries. This is unacceptable! Little do they know that this situation also has its actual social roots. Whether you like it or not, as long as these actual social roots exist, the literary phenomena produced by them will always exist and develop.

The Disappearance of Honoré Shoubrak (1) 187

— Written by G. Apollinaire of France Translated by Xiao Lin

Although the police conducted a very detailed investigation into the disappearance of Honoré Shoubrak, the incredible truth about this incident could not be ascertained, and so it was dealt with perfunctorily.

Honoré Shoubrak was my friend, and I also knew the whole story of this incident very well, so I believed that reporting the truth of this matter to the authorities was my duty. But after the judge finished listening to my statement, he actually questioned me with an extraordinary gentle tone. Therefore, I knew that this judge actually regarded me as a madman. I pointed this out to the judge. But by doing so, he became even more gentle. And before long, he suddenly stood up and quickly pushed me towards the door. Even the clerk who had just been copying my statement also stood up arrogantly, clenching his fists as if I would suddenly pounce on him if I went crazy, posing in such a fierce manner.

After this, I no longer insisted on saying anything. In short, the disappearance of Honoré Shoubrak was indeed too bizarre, resulting in the truth resembling a groundless fabrication. Shoubrak was originally a strange character, as reported in the news articles at the time of his disappearance. No matter the time, regardless of winter or summer, he was always naked except for a monk's robe, and on his equally bare feet, he wore a pair of slippers. Knowing that he was very wealthy, I found this unbelievable and had asked him why he dressed so indecently in public. His reply at the time was like this:

— This is in preparation for being able to quickly transform into a nude state when necessary. As for wearing thin clothing outdoors, the human body can easily get used to it. I have abolished all clothing articles such as trousers, shirts, hats, and socks. I have been living like this since I was twenty-five years old and have not even been sick once.

However, these words not only did not explain my doubts in the slightest, but instead pricked up my curiosity.

— What does this mean after all? Why does Honoré Shoubrak need to quickly undress and return to a nude state?

I had to think this way.

One late night, when I was returning home—around one or one fifteen in the morning—I heard someone softly calling my name; and the voice seemed to be coming from the wall I had brushed past. I was startled and unconsciously stopped. The voice then continued:

— Can't you see anyone on the street? It's me, Honoré Shoubrak.

I opened my eyes and looked around, but I couldn't find my friend's shadow there.

— Where exactly are you? I said.

At this moment, I saw the familiar monk's robe and the pair of slippers on the sidewalk.

— This must be a situation where Honoré Shoubrak had to quickly undress due to some necessity. This time, I must grasp the key to his secret. Thinking this, I shouted:

— There's no one on the street. My friend, come out.

Honoré Shoubrak suddenly appeared naked from the wall I couldn't see anything just now. He quickly put on the monk's robe from over his head, hurriedly buttoned it up, and then put on the pair of slippers. With a resolute expression, he walked straight towards my door with me, walking side by side while speaking.

A Melancholy Patient 188

— Ding

It has only been a short two years since Jane became a nun. Yet everything has changed so quickly.

Wasn't Jane a robust, lively, beautiful, and capable woman when she was still studying at the provincial high school the year before last?

At that time, Jane was not only talkative, liked to read, and willing to work, but also liked to exercise.

She was truly optimistic about life. Therefore, she held a strong pursuit and lofty ideals for everything in the future. How lovely and glorious Jane was.

I remember—that was on the evening when we were about to part ways, Jane stood in the center of the student union's podium and spoke to us sternly, resolutely, cautiously, and seemingly as a farewell message: "We are considered to have graduated. After this, there will be very few opportunities for everyone to gather together, talk, and work together. Therefore, at this time, while we have not yet dispersed, I want to sincerely talk to everyone. I feel that our task will be even more arduous after this. After leaving the school gate and stepping into society, everything will not be the same as in school. We must understand what a terrible situation China—especially our women—is currently in. We seem to be living inhuman lives. Everything makes us feel heartbroken and resentful! Therefore, as women of the new era, we should take on a great mission! We must fight against the adverse environment surrounding us. We cannot be like ordinary "modern" women who only indulge in rosy lives and that kind of despicable behavior that specializes in catering to male psychology. We should bring out the spirit of the new century—self-respect, independence, progress, and struggle—and go ahead with our consistent purpose. At the very least, among our millions of female compatriots, we must lead them, awaken them, and open up a path for our miserable fate! This is my last conversation with all of you. In the future, if there is an opportunity, I hope that everyone can supervise each other, be diligent, help each other, and often instruct me!"

However, after only a short two years of separation, Jane's change is so sudden and rapid.

Since then, Jane has only been sitting dully at home in silence all day long, not going out, not doing things, not reading books, and even being too lazy to speak. All day long, she is either dozing or playing cards. If she is not playing cards, she quietly sits alone in a daze by the south-facing window, gazing dreamily at the azure sky and the bright moon. Her heart is melancholy, like the autumn season.

"How is this kind of life passing by in depression!" she muttered. Then she sighed deeply and looked out the window again. The azure sky was full of twinkling stars, and the earth was still lying in the deathly silence of the moonlight. And in the shadow of the thatched cottage vaguely in this deathly moonlight, as well as the desolate and mournful coughs, made Jane even more distressed. At this time, a hot, painful, and seemingly sun-scorched stone-like thought surged in her mind. Faced with this thought, Jane could not use an appropriate, coherent, and clear sentence to explain it.

"Oh, forget it. Look, look!" Jane muttered to herself, "How beautiful, noble, lovely, and glorious this moon is." Then, a difficult joy appeared on Jane's face. And this joy, if you carefully taste the ingredients inside, you will find that it is such a bitter joy.

Perhaps, it can be said that this voice is a passion reversed from Jane's vitality. This voice may be an understanding of the beauty of nature and love experienced from Jane's long-term immersion in a life of suffering. In short, Jane has changed now, everything has changed, consciously and physically.

In the past, those noble, proud, and glorious qualities have quietly slipped away from Jane's life.

Now Jane is so lonely and depressed, staying in a daze like an idiot in a dark house, gazing at the lonely sky and the lonely summer moon. Only in such a blue night does Jane feel how melancholy the heart of a lonely person is.

"Life is so boring!" Then a sentimental tear wet her clothes. "Oh, I really regret leaving school! Why didn't I go on to university? Why did I marry such an ugly old man? Am I crazy? Have I lost all my sanity? Oh, why? Money? Fame? Enjoyment? What a cursed thing this is! Isn't this weak and greedy old man a person I often despise? Isn't he the kind of guy who relies on his strong financial power to seduce, oppress, play with, and trample on us women? Huh, huh! How could I marry him!..." With a condemning tone, Jane questioned herself so indignantly.

However, everything seemed irreparable. Since her father's business failed, Jane had no possibility of continuing her studies due to the family's financial constraints. Since then, Jane's life has undergone many changes. But in the end, finally under her father's stern threats and her mother's bitter pleas, Jane inexplicably agreed and succumbed. She married a man who had once been cited by Jane as a point of attack, a playboy who relied on his ancestors' inheritance to live a degenerate life.

But—"That's so strange?" Jane said, "Are my eyes blind too? This is clearly an ugly fat merchant! Oh, I was deceived, I was fooled. Everything—is over! I... I am sacrificed under a social system that worships money and honor..."

Jane then sobbed convulsively.

After enduring such a miserable life for only two years, Jane seemed like a dying person, or like a pair of broken shoes, thrown into some corner.

From the cold world, she gained a contempt of regret; from hypocritical exchanges, she felt a heartbreaking pain; from the arrogant, she received an unbearable cold shoulder; from her past classmates, she was ashamed of the disgrace of her life! From the old man, she sensed a capitalist's rancid and savage smell.

"No! No! I absolutely cannot go on like this," Jane finally shouted involuntarily.

— Written by Hu Kao

Flour prices fluctuated yesterday, initially rising before falling. The price of foreign wheat from Chicago improved by 8 fen to 1 jiao, while Canadian wheat remained unchanged. Prices were slightly better for foreign wheat at the opening, which gave people confidence in the market's stability. Early-month prices were similar to the previous day. Afterward, prices gradually increased as speculators made some transactions, with the closing price reaching 5 jiao 2 fen 7 li and a half. Prices for June and July also rose slightly due to sluggish trading, increasing by 1 fen. Prices for September and October remained stable with little fluctuation. However, prices fell sharply in the afternoon's opening, with near-term contracts declining across the board. With the arrival of new wheat approaching this month, demand from inland buyers, except those in the north, was weak, leading to speculation that the price of foreign wheat would fall further, with Australian wheat quoted at 6 jiao 2 fen. There were also rumors that inland factories had already made an order for a ship, which dampened market sentiment, and prices fell step by step. Considering the cheap price of foreign wheat, factories are likely to place orders one after another, making it difficult to be overly optimistic about the future of the flour market. As a result, the price for this month fell by 1 fen 7 li and a half, June fell by 1 fen 7 li and a half, July fell by 1 fen, August fell by half a fen, September fell by 7 li and a half, and October fell by 1 fen 2 li and a half.

Yesterday's wheat futures market was calm in the morning but fell sharply in the afternoon. Chicago's foreign wheat prices were slightly better by 8 fen to 1 jiao, while Canadian wheat was suspended. Trading was not active at the opening, with prices fluctuating due to a lack of sellers, showing little change from the previous day. The market initially appeared stable in the afternoon opening, but the powder market declined because it was reported that Australian wheat was cheaper than ever. Though no deal was certain at 4.6 jiao or 4.6 jiao, 1 fen, it shocked the market because of rumors of the new wheat to be harvested next time and the imports of wheat were as cheap. There are many changes in the future.
