Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 200

— (Sun Lang)

People must eat, so they must work: if they didn't eat, why work? If they didn't work, where would the food come from?

Only eating and not working is a stupid pig; greedy for food and afraid of work is a lazy worm; eating and working, working and eating, can be called a human being.

A beggar who has been begging will only show a smile after death; or he is thanking God for removing the root of his pain.

The hands of the rich only consume; the hands of the poor are what produce; therefore, the more poor people there are in the world, the greater the productivity.

Generous food and warm clothing are the poison of youth,

Broad Beans 201

— Qing Qu

The broad bean is also called "cold bean" because this plant was originally herbaceous, but it is biennial (science divides it into annual, biennial, or perennial). Now, if you plant the seeds this year (around mid-August or September), they will only mature when raising silkworms next year. Don't you think it has passed two years? Therefore, judging from the bean's name, it has survived the cold winter without freezing to death, so it is called "cold bean." Its flowers are like small butterflies dancing on the branches, showing a purple-black beauty in the swaying spring breeze, pleasing to the eye. But when it forms the fruit, it is called the "bean pod," about three inches long and green in color, with a layer of snow-white fluff inside, almost like wadding, and there are three or four beans, like silkworms sleeping peacefully inside. When it is half-ripe, the front of the bean's embryo also reveals a curved black line, which looks very much like "moth eyebrows"; hence it is called "broad bean," which is really not bad!

There are two types of "broad beans" produced in my hometown: one is called "Green Cold," and the other is called "White Cold." If you eat them when they are tender, "White Cold" is naturally the best. Because "White Cold" has finer and softer meat, cooks quickly in a pot, and has thinner skin with no astringent taste, it is especially delicious. Like "Green Cold," its texture is hard. If it is dry and old, whether it is stir-fried or made into bean paste, it is no different from other vegetables. In the current vegetable foods, "White Cold" is always the best. "Broad beans" are on the market earliest in Guangdong, followed by Zhejiang. The ones eaten in Shanghai restaurants in February of the lunar calendar are mostly from Guangdong, followed by Zhejiang. The warmer the climate, the earlier the production. Like Jiading, they are just now coming on the market, which is the latest. Moreover, "White Cold" only grows in the villages near the city. If you go five or six miles outside the city, the "cold beans" in the fields all become "Green Cold," which is also very strange. Perhaps it is a change in the seed and the relationship with the soil; there is no other reason!

Quick Sketch on Bus Route 10 202

— Zhang Muliang

Among the bus routes in the concession, Route 10 is probably the longest. It runs from Caojiadu in West Shanghai to Yinxianggang in East Shanghai. The two places it connects are both industrial areas, and the journey is about thirty li long.

It is rare to see wealthy old men and coquettish aristocratic women here. What you can see are people from all walks of life and the working class. Because of this, there is basically no order or hygiene. The noise and swirling smoke will really make people feel unbearable and want to vomit!

But here there are rare interesting stories, novel jokes... endless, it is a source of jokes.

The ticket seller seemed to recognize that Jiangbei woman and said: "Hurry up! Hurry up! You always drag your feet and bargain when you buy a ticket; we ticket sellers are not selling vegetables."

"Oh! Sir! A small matter of two coppers refund, why are you making such a fuss?"

"Damn your mother—you lost the coppers yourself and you're blaming me for making a fuss?" the ticket seller said, also speaking in the Jiangbei dialect.

That Jiangbei woman had long been angered by the ticket seller's words, so she rushed forward and slapped the ticket seller in the face, saying: "You want money and should speak nicely, why are you scolding people? I'll hit your cobbler's sign!" The ticket seller was not willing to show weakness. Moreover, after being slapped twice, he became even more enraged. Without listening to the Jiangbei woman's words, he also rudely beat the Jiangbei woman. As a result, everyone fought regardless of everything, and the order was completely disrupted. Fortunately, several peacemakers came out to smooth things over, and they all said in unison: "Okay! Okay! Everyone, don't quarrel anymore..."

This storm had just subsided when another storm came. A country bumpkin-like person, who had been sitting in the back corner of the bus sleeping, heard that Xiaoshadu Road had arrived, so he rushed out in a hurry. The Russian ticket inspector wanted to see his ticket. He had bought an eleven-cent ticket, and the Russian ticket inspector also seemed to recognize him. So, speaking in pure Chinese, he said: "You only bought eleven cents from Yinxianggang to here?"

"Mr. Russian! I fell asleep and forgot to get off. Thank you for letting me get off!"

"You are very bad. You always want to freeload. I met you at Xiaoshadu Road last time, pretending to be asleep, trying to get away with it. Today, pretending to be asleep is not allowed. I won't fine you for the ticket, but please get off at Caojiadu..."

This Russian ticket inspector's eyesight is really good. At the same time, his method of fining tickets is also very unique. He asked the friend who pretended to be asleep to get off at Caojiadu. Of course, this friend would have to go back to Xiaoshadu Road, so wouldn't the fare from Caojiadu to Xiaoshadu be equal to a fine? A laugh.

In short, there are many jokes on Bus Route 10, and some of them are unbelievable.

The Drifting Record of Imperial Fragrance 204

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

Sometimes, the Empress Dowager would linger in this Imperial Dog Kennel for a long time: in addition to having the pugs perform for her as usual, she would also randomly designate a dog to be inspected. Of course, Her Old Highness would never deign to squat down to get close to them. The eunuch in charge of the dogs would always have to pick up the dog she designated, hold it up in front of her, and let her examine it carefully. After examining it, she would always say, "Its eyes are too dirty. Are you not taking care of things? You must pay attention to it in the future!" Or, "This dog's hind legs are too long, or too short, not the right size!" Or, "This dog's body is too long. It's too ugly!" After she gave one of these two comments to any dog—especially newborn puppies—it was as if they had received an order of exile and could no longer live in the palace. They had to be banished immediately. Because hind legs that were too long or too short, as well as bodies that were too long, were incurable defects, they had to be asked to leave. However, the eunuchs in charge of the dogs, to avoid trouble, often simply killed the dogs that had been ordered to be banished. Fortunately, the Empress Dowager would not investigate. But when it was a puppy that was being banished, they were not willing to kill it easily. They would secretly carry it out of the palace and sell it to acquaintances. The price was often considerable, because people knew that it was a dog brought out of the palace and were particularly eager to have it, so they were willing to pay more.

On this day, we had originally come to see the four puppies born by "Black Jade"; therefore, the eunuch in charge of the dogs hurriedly presented them in a bamboo basket. (316)

Miscellaneous Remarks

Reading Notes on Paintings (Part 1) - Regarding Objects from the Former Palace Museum to be Exhibited in England; 205

— Xu Bangda

Dong Yuan's "Dragon Dwelling Among Suburban People" (絹本大樻幅, silk scroll, large format), an old painting cherished by Zen masters, is considered as precious as "Autumn Mountains of Xiaoxiang." I have long admired it and finally had the opportunity to see it. The painting depicts layered peaks and valleys, with houses along the cliffs adorned with lanterns and colorful decorations. The residents appear to be dancing and rejoicing, conveying the idea of "Emperor Taizu descending to Jiangnan, with people offering food and drink to welcome the royal army." However, the inscription by Mo Jing mentions "rich and magnificent pavilions and terraces," which are not present in this version. Could there be another copy? The *cun* method (texturing strokes) uses broad "hemp fiber" strokes. The nearby trees are elegantly rendered with clustered dots and interspersed leaves. The mountaintops are depicted with small horizontal dots, differing from later Northern School followers who only used "nail-head" or round dots. The use of green and blue colors is especially unique and antique. A distant mountain is rendered in emerald green, giving a bright and pleasing effect. Ju Ran's "Cold Forest and Evening Peaks" still has good brushwork, but lacks an antique quality, likely a creation of a Yuan or Ming master. It doesn't compare to the true Ju Ran. I haven't seen any paintings by Yiying, but I've seen Fan Kuan and Guo Xi. Fan Kuan's large hanging scroll "Solitary Seated Figure by a Stream" is not good. Guo Xi's "Spring Snow on Mountains and Streams" is better, but "High Hermitage in a Mountain Villa" is not in the style of a Northern Song artist, lacking the rustic and integrated effect. The brushwork in the colored landscape is almost slippery at the corners where the lines bend, so it's not a painting by Xi. Su Hanchen's two paintings, "Autumn Garden Infants at Play" and "Peddler," are both excellent, especially "Infants at Play." One infant stands opposite another, one dressed in red, the other in white. The lines of the clothing are vigorous and rounded, the facial features are bright, and the lakeside rocks and autumn flowers are elegantly outlined and colored. A truly wonderful piece. Ma Hezhi's "Leisurely and Busy" is particularly bad. Liu Songnian's "Five Scholars" has good brushwork, but is not necessarily by Liu. "Silk Thread Drawing" is by a Ming artist. "Pavilion Second, the Four Pleasures" is a truly remarkable work of the Southern Song dynasty. The rocks are rendered with axe-cut strokes, with sharp edges protruding in all directions. The outlines of the pine bark are dense and weighty, and the houses and figures are all skillfully executed with precision and discipline. Among the three scrolls by Ma Xia, only "Willow Boats on West Lake" with a colophon by Guo Tianxi is relatively good. Qin Shan's painting, such as "Viewing the Moon," is a forgery. "Ten Thousand Miles of the Yangtze River Scroll" is by a Ming artist who studied the Northern School. The chopped strokes are weak and unconvincing, and the flow of the water is particularly lacking in freedom and dynamism. How could it be a painting by Gui? Qian Yutan's "Autumn Melon" is vaguely wonderful but I cannot recall in detail. Among the albums of Song and Yuan paintings, Qian Yutan's "Wild Fragrant Stone Fist" is the finest, and the paper is also pristine. Zhou Yuesu's "Yuanming Drunk" still has elegance. There are as many as eighteen Song paintings without inscriptions. Among them, "Loquat and Monkey Playing" is the best, almost on par with Yi Yuanji and his school. Zhao Mengfu's "Layered Mountains and Overlapping Peaks Scroll" is in the style of Guo Heyang. The texture strokes and ink washes resemble cursive script, and the small trees and dots of foliage are like piled cotton. The gentle hills reflect the slopes and rocks, creating an irregular composition. At the end of the scroll, two tall and elegant pine trees are depicted, with a small *kaishu* inscription reading: "Painted by Zhao Mengfu of Wuxing on the sixth day of the second month of the seventh year of Dade." In the upper right corner, there are five characters for the painting title, of which three are damaged. It is a first-class Yuan painting, a divine masterpiece that can be treasured alongside "Autumn Colors of Quehua." Zhu Zemin's "Playing Zither Beneath the Forest" is painted in the same style as Heyang, but lacks the refined, elegant and bold appeal. Huang Zijiu and Gao Fangshan's paintings are both ugly and crude. Fang Fanghu also has no fine works. Yifeng's "Dwelling in the Fuchun Mountains," said to be the remaining section after the cloud-rising building burned down, is particularly clumsy and laughable. There are probably dozens of copies of this scroll, which will lead to many disputes. I don't know where Emperor Zhaoling's ancestral calligraphy copy is now. When I look at Shigu Zi's late-year copy, it is better than this one. Emperor Gaozong of Qing Dynasty's imperial inscription takes up all empty space, the songs and praises are dreamlike. Cao Yunxi's "Double Pines," Ke Danqiu's "Bamboo and Rocks," Wu Zhong'sheng's "Fisherman's Hermitage in Dongting," and Wang Shuming's "Eastern Mountain Thatched Cottage" are all fake and bad pieces. Only Shan Qiao has "Spring Plowing in Gukou," which completely imitates Dong Yuan and Ju Ran's hemp-fiber *cun*. Siweng's inscription says it is similar to our family's "Qingbian Painting," which is excellent, ancient and simple, following the path of his uncle, the paper is slightly worn, fortunately not damaging the painting. Mei Daoren's large silk painting, titled "Double Pine Trees," is good, but they are old cypresses, not Qin Daifu. The bamboo and rocks are also simple and elegant. Although Sheng Zizhao's "Autumn Forest High Scholar" cannot be compared to Zhonggui in terms of its elevated quality, it is still worthy of respect due to its strict adherence to the rules and regulations. The red-clothed person under the forest still retains the charm of the Tang and Song dynasties. Later generations criticized Zhonggui for living across from him, which is an overcorrection. Yunlin Zi's "Mountain View from the Riverbank" is extremely good, with vigorous brushstrokes and a tall peak with long *cun* strokes stretching straight down, surpassing Jing Hao and Guan Tong and entering the Northern Yuan style. How can we use the Ni Zan method of superimposed cakes and folded belts to paint? This scroll was painted for the recluse Wei Yun, so it is free and unrestrained. The "Narrow Room" is slightly restrained, but also elegant and beautiful. Gu Dingzhi and Zhang Yunmen jointly wrote about bamboo and trees, which Yang Lianfu inscribed. I don't know how, on the right side, there is a row of cloud forest rocks and long sentences, the inscription "Tongxuan recluse Ni Yu," the calligraphy is inferior, and Yu Weng's Yu, is it really self-proclaimed? If so, then Fan Kuan and Mi Dian can all write large scrolls. Gu Zhang's pen is a wonderful work, and Tie Sui Daoren is also only a small note. Lu Tianyou's "Five Auspicious Symbols" is a follower of the Wu School during the Zhengjia period, filling in the details. Zhang Shunzi, a Yuan person, is not very well-known, but the small scroll of trees and rocks is quite good. Li Shixing, whose courtesy name is Zundao, is the descendant of Xi Qi. The large painting of pine and stones is very strange. The basket beside the stone also reflects the family style. Wu Tinghui's "Dragon Boat Racing" is very exquisite. It is said that Hu Tinghui is old, not knowing if they are the same person? Guo Tianxi wrote the poetry intention of Gao Shijun, the painting is very ancient and beautiful, but it is not like a Yuan person's pen, if Wang Gengyan, it is almost close. Chen Xiaoran's "Jingxi Map," the silk is broken, the mountains and rocks are all studying Dong Yuan and Ju Ran, below are countless houses facing the stream, and there are dozens of inscriptions, Yunlin Zi Shang Zuo Sheng Wang Shuming Zhou Lvdiao, the rest I don't remember, all are famous scholars of the time.

Little Western Paradise 206

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirteen: It’s Difficult to Provide a Dowry, Pitiful to Sell One’s Body; Enslaved to Merchandise, Joyful; Bankrupted, Talking of Farming Life

As he pondered this, he had some ideas. So he turned around and asked Yueying again: "Why have you been waiting for us here for so long?" Yueying said: "Mr. Cheng's things in the house are all scattered. Mr. Cheng hasn't returned to his room, how could I dare to leave?" Zhiqian said: "What you say doesn't make sense. If we didn't come back until evening, would you wait until evening? Also, Miss Yang and your aunt, Hu Saozi, are both careless. How can they leave a young lady like you here by yourself?" Yueying said: "They went to apologize to Mr. Jia in front because he was unhappy." Zhiqian said: "Why was Mr. Jia unhappy? Is it because you missed your appointment and didn't accompany him to dinner?" Yueying lowered her head and hummed softly through her nose, indicating that he was right. When Zhiqian looked at Beihai again, he saw that his face was also red, as if he was also a little ashamed of this matter. So he sighed and said: "Judging by your character, you have a good path to follow. However, your family burdens you too much, preventing you from living comfortably and starving the two generations above you. Because of the two generations above you, you naturally have to suffer some grievances in the present. But thinking long-term, suffering a little grievance temporarily doesn't amount to much." Zhiqian first stated this grand principle, intending to continue with more words. However, Wang Beihai, sitting under the wall inside, couldn't bear it anymore and interjected: "That can't be said that way. If a person endures a little grievance temporarily for the sake of their career and then seeks development, that's understandable." (206)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Chinese Egg Problem and Others 207

— Qiong Sheng

I don't know if it was because George Bernard Shaw was born in England, or if England produced George Bernard Shaw, but in any case, the gentlemen who come from this country all speak with great humor, which is very pleasant. The year before last, Mr. Shaw traveled to the Far East as part of a tour group. Newspaper reporters in Beiping, Tokyo, and other places asked him about the situation in the Far East. The old man's reply was that it was inconvenient to talk here and there was no freedom of speech there. This attitude was, of course, full of humor. But in the parliament in London, British gentlemen would not feel "inconvenient" or "unfree," and they could speak frankly. However, they still displayed their unique nature—humor.

Last year, a member of the British House of Commons questioned Japan's refusal to allow foreign troops to conduct exercises in the Yuguan area, saying it violated treaties, and asked whether Britain had protested. Simon replied that it was not so important that exercises could not be held in Yuguan, as there were many places inside the pass where exercises could be held. The entire hall burst into laughter. It was praised as "humorous." Recently, because of rumors that imported Chinese eggs contained bacteria, the House paid special attention and discussed the matter, resulting in another "humorous" story.

A Reuters dispatch from London on the 13th stated: "Sasby, representing the Minister of Health, said that recent research focused on the bacterial content of Chinese eggs. He heard that eggs did not decompose when they were removed from the ice. Han Lun said that Chinese eggs were produced under conditions that made people nauseous and should be banned from import immediately. Labor MP Lawson said that the living standards of Chinese chickens were actually lower than those of American chickens, which caused a burst of laughter in the hall."

In the eyes of gentlemen and ladies from various powers, there are many things in China that are in a "nauseating state." Japanese people talking about "Nanjing bugs" in China, Western European museums displaying "three-inch golden lotuses," Americans saying that Chinese people eat snakes—all of this is their impression of Chinese people. Not only that, but among "civilized people," it is often said that the Chinese nation lives in filthy mud like pigs and breeds like rats. The "Chinatown" of New York and the "Chinese Quarter" of Tokyo are mentioned with frowns and disgusted expressions, "making people nauseous." Therefore, we can imagine that the restrictions and exclusion of overseas Chinese in various countries are perhaps because Chinese people, like Chinese eggs, are nauseating, and therefore "banned from import"?

If that is the case, we can also "humorously" say, according to Lawson's words, "The living standards of Chinese people are actually lower than those of Americans." But why are the living standards of Chinese people lower than those of Americans? Isn't this the obvious result of the powers' aggression? However, the gentlemen and ladies of various countries understand humor, so they cannot say the "unhumorous" following words.

Sea Voyage 208

— Hua Gong

What a treacherous voyage! A violent wind was blowing, with fine rain falling like broken threads. The waves were surging, hitting the tossing ship's body, creating a clamorous noise that echoed the sound of the engine below.

The remaining currents and splashes fiercely entered the cabin from the openings. Passengers huddled in the cramped and overflowing third-class cabin felt uneasy, threatened by the great force of nature, directly sensing the insignificance of life and the strange terror of death.

Page 18

Three to five dim lights were the only source of illumination, shining on the narrow wooden planks that served as beds, so cramped that they could barely accommodate a person, like various goods displayed in a shop window, separated by wooden boards.

Looking out from the cabin opening, the gloomy clouds and hazy sky, along with the raging waves, resembled an endless, infinitely simple ink painting, making people shiver.

Inside the cabin, bluish-gray, murky dust rose, weaving a heavy, terrifying veil. Thin, small creatures, like miscellaneous goods, gasped for breath within this veil.

On the second day of the sea voyage, near evening, the ship docked at a port.

People crawled out of the veil one by one, staggering and pacing on the deck. The treacherous voyage of the past two days had painted the same expression on everyone's face: pale, ashen, heads lowered on their chests, feet unusually weak, eyelids swollen and protruding.

The rain had stopped at some unknown time, and the sea breeze had become moist and gentle, with a cool, damp feeling all around. Under the heavy, low-hanging clouds, the dark waves rose and fell gently. In the distance, the sky met the water in a vast, misty expanse, with continuous mountains standing tall like screens on the sea. The darkness of night settled in.

People also regained their inherent reserve. The solemn gentlemen in first class chatted quietly, and occasionally a faint, clear laugh from a woman floated down. The laughter stirred the figures beneath the veil, and the jumbled dialects and kind-hearted curses began.

Enchanting music came from the deck above. Standing on the deck and looking up, under the brilliant lights, noble men and women each occupied a seat, chewing on things and dancing in pairs.

"Even in the most difficult places to adapt to nature, like a sea voyage, people are still separated far apart..." Similar vague feelings of melancholy rose unconsciously, and with excessive fatigue and厭心, each person repeated the cramming into the suffocating veil, curled up in the corner of the original board, and then remembered the forgotten ups and downs of family, saturated through the vicissitudes of the quiet heart wave, then set off the seeds of vagrant's bitter flavor.

The ship's body moved slightly to the side, the wet sea breeze blew in from the cabin opening, also bringing in charming music, the sound of water lapping lapping. Unbearable silence of the heart拘起 various thoughts.

Yearning Under the Sea 209

— Luo Jia

I know that the sea is full of pain. When it rolls up a snow-white wave, and then rolls up another snow-white wave, it gently caresses the ochre-yellow shoreline, lamenting its unbearable sorrow.

(Yes! The sea is full of pain. At the pier, where colorful ribbons, handkerchiefs, and hats are waving, the Victoria, having just sailed off for a long voyage across the ocean, and the Comtesse Roussot, saturated with Parisian powder, are slowly entering! These enormous monsters carry thousands of tons of sorrowful separation! Those thousands of lines of bitter, sour tears of longing for distant loved ones gently seep into the heart of the sea, causing it to be forever sad! Forever sad! Its lament will never cease!)

And I also know that the sea is hardworking. When the sea fog blocks the clear light of the moon at night, and sprinkles down on the fishing boats with their single, flickering lights, the sea appears extremely desolate. Then, the sea sighs wearily, the sound is desolate and sobbing!

(Yes! The sea is hardworking. The sea is the greatest manual laborer, flowing its own blood day and night, nurturing countless lives—those fishermen and salt makers. They live by the enormous production of the seabed. Therefore, the sea is too hardworking! It has no leisure time, never wiping away sweat or shedding tears. Although it has sighed wearily!)

I am—a child who has failed the sea's love.

However, only I understand the sea, because I am a child of the sea. My body has been nurtured by the sea, my soul has been陶冶 by the sea. Therefore, I love the sea, just as I love my mother.

I grew up in a fishing village by the sea. I am familiar with the sea's cough, the sea's breath, and its pain, its hard work. I often offer heartfelt blessings.

When I tied my hair into two small buns (at that time, I only knew the sweetness of sugar and did not like the salty bitterness of salt!), I often spent the entire day at the beach. I knew how to pick a few wild flowers and grasses and insert them into the soft sand that had just been kissed by the sea, and hold solemn wild sacrifices with my little friends. I knew how to wait for the tide to recede and collect beautiful shells on the soft beach. Even though my hands were already full, the impression that the shells gave us was too enticing! Forcing me to take off the large straw hat I was wearing on my head and bring it home full of shells. I often gave my most beloved shells to my little sister, because my little sister was a shell collector. Or we would sit elegantly on the rocks by the sea, knowing how to gaze at the fishing boats floating and sinking in the waves. Watching white-feathered water birds sweep over our heads and fly into the sea. Paying attention to the purple and white clouds in the sky, transforming into a tree, a garden of spring flowers, a divine dragon, a red horse.

In this way, I grew up in the sea's brilliance. I believe that the time I spent in my mother's arms was less than the days I spent on the beach! The sea is my mother, my nanny!

However, I have failed the sea's love. It endowed me with the unique temperament of a coastal resident, but I could not use them one by one. Even more, in order to adapt to my environment, I compromised and hid them in the secret room of my heart!

Is it still lamenting unbearable sorrow? Is it still sighing wearily? My great mother, my yearning for you is too bitter and too heavy! Even in my dreams.

Miss Qin 210

— Ting Yi

Red and gold posters flew all over the street, announcing Miss Qin's debut at the Hongxing Teahouse. The owner of the Hongxing Teahouse was a well-respected figure. Every day, when he carried his birdcage from home to the teahouse, some people nodded to him, and some called him "Boss." He always casually inclined his head, grinding the pair of walnuts in his other hand with a clattering sound. But he treated those teahouse patrons with a different attitude. Because although he was called "Boss" of the Hongxing Teahouse, it was the local gentry and wealthy merchants who had taken out their wallets to organize this club-style teahouse. The owner naturally had to use his skills to deal with those masters who were like his providers. Miss Qin's performance at the Hongxing Teahouse was one of the owner's strategies to please those masters.

Before the sun had set, the large billboard in front of the Hongxing Teahouse, along with the major local shops, lit up the three large characters "Miss Qin" in electric lights. The owner personally greeted guests at the door, his fat face piled with fleshy wrinkles, his eyes naturally appearing even smaller, but his undeniable large belly protruded high outside his silk shirt. He smiled proudly, the pair of walnuts echoing the beating of his heart.

Upstairs, the four walls were hung with silk banners presented to Miss Qin by various masters, including various praises such as "Celestial Being Transformed" and "Clear Singing and Wonderful Dance." Rattan chairs were added along the walls, which were exclusively for the actual owners of the teahouse. The square tables in the center were for selling seats to outside guests. But now seats were also arranged next to the stairs. The owner's forehead was covered with large beads of sweat, as he moved from one master to another, sometimes speaking softly. As a result, everyone's face was full of smiles.

The electric lights on a plaque on the stage also lit up. It was a special gift to Miss Qin from Master Hu, who held the top position in the local area. On it was a poem, specially made to order from a Xiang Embroidery shop in Shanghai. For this grand gift, the owner accompanied Miss Qin to Master Hu's mansion last night to express their gratitude in person.

The scene became lively. The entire Hongxing Teahouse was disturbed by the noise. Countless pairs of eyes were focused on the embroidered curtain. Amidst a burst of enthusiastic applause, Miss Qin gracefully emerged from behind the curtain. She swept her gaze around, deliberately feigning a smile with a silk scarf covering the corner of her mouth. The masters couldn't help but clap their hands.

The *huqin* played the prelude for the second time. Miss Qin sang "Si Lang Visits His Mother," which Master Hu had personally requested last night.

The one called Master Hu sat on the side of the stage next to the wall. He was the first to receive Miss Qin's seductive gaze. Now he contentedly closed his eyes slightly, tapping the armrest of the rattan chair with the index finger, middle finger, and ring finger of his right hand. The leg resting on his left knee also swung naturally. At the end of each drawn-out phrase, he immediately clapped his hands together, but his enthusiasm was drowned out by the louder applause.

After Miss Qin finished singing, she picked up the golden teapot to moisten her throat. The owner, looking like a short, fat winter melon, rolled over to Master Hu again, humbly asking him to request a play. Master Hu secretly surveyed everyone to maintain his own dignity. He refused with a smile. So a folded note was passed to the second master, the third, the fourth... Everyone politely smiled and declined. At this moment, a loud voice flew out from the crowd:

"Sing Wujia Slope!"

No one had the leisure to investigate the source of this voice. Master Hu was the first to clap his hands, and naturally a series of applause rang out.

As usual, Miss Qin swept her gaze around the four walls, tapped her toes to the beat, and began to sing "Wujia Slope." In the second section, she put in extra effort, singing as Xue Pinggui, forcing her false voice to sing Wang Baochuan. The applause was like thunder, sending her back behind the embroidered curtain.

The audience was unwilling to leave immediately, their gazes all shooting toward the back of the stage. Some part of them had been captured by Miss Qin's flirtatious eyes. The owner bowed deeply, asking the masters to come earlier tomorrow.

As the guests left one after another, the owner flew to the backstage like a swallow, whispering in the ear of Miss Qin, who was taking off her makeup: "Master Hu is inviting you." At the same time, he gave the deputy town a hard to look at媚眼.

Uncle Yuan 211

— Li Qing

In the morning, at half-past six, everyone had already finished breakfast and gathered in the courtyard to pick mulberry leaves. The silkworms had awakened from their great sleep and started eating leaves. In another three or four days, they would be ready to spin cocoons. However, at this time, their appetite was enormous. Piles and piles of mulberry leaves were laid down, and immediately a rustling sound arose, like a sudden rain, sounding very clear and frequent.

Because the consumption of mulberry leaves was so fast, everyone picking mulberry leaves was working hard.

Especially in the morning, the first batch after the dew had dried was clipped the most. The courtyard was piled high, full, and children and adults were all working; this lively scene was still a first this year.

While working, they chatted idly to resist fatigue, a common strategy for physical laborers. So, Uncle Yuan's bragging started again.

First, Ah Kun mentioned planting melons, and Uncle Yuan said, full of spirit:

——In recent years, fewer people are planting melons. Hey, Ah Kun, you didn't see it, but seven or eight years ago, the watermelons in front of Chen Family Village were so big! So lush, Ah Si and I would always get one or two loads in one night!

Aunt Yuan then chimed in: ——Stealing melons, what kind of good thing is that? You're still talking about it so loudly!

But Uncle Yuan didn't care at all and continued to talk on and on, and Ah Kun and Ah Mao also joined in, boasting about their skills in stealing melons. They thought: "Stealing melons doesn't count as stealing."

Before long, Long-Legged Ah San returned from the street with a piglet. He brought people an ominous message:

——This year's silkworm prices are unreasonable again. Both cocoon merchants want to open, but I heard the highest price is only twenty yuan per batch. The villagers are really on their way to ruin!

Many people's faces were covered with worry. Only someone as muddleheaded as Uncle Yuan was still enthusiastically saying:

——It really can't compare to before! A few years ago,

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

eight or nine years ago, Ah Mao, you didn't see it! The cocoon merchants were packed so tightly that no air could get through, and no one could squeeze in, let alone selling cocoons! Many people from the sandbars would come before dawn, wanting to take advantage? Bargain, how easy would that be? People there wouldn't let you squeeze in, and there were many stronger than you. And the locals only helped the locals, why would they help you sandbar people? Ah, it was really sinful to watch, they waited until sunset and still hadn't sold them, their stomachs growling with hunger, and they didn't have any money to buy snacks, so they could only prostrate themselves on the bridge and cry like women! Crying, crying to death, no one would pay attention to them!

Before everyone could express their opinions, Uncle Yuan continued impatiently:

——Cocoons used to be expensive, seventy or eighty yuan per load. There were benefits, so naturally, there were more people raising silkworms. To be honest, back then, only Ah Pe and I sold cocoons in the village, squeezing in and squeezing out. Selling for ourselves and selling for others, who was fierce? A punch! Retaliate? Hmph, don't even think about it! Unless he didn't want to sell his cocoons for money! …

Uncle Yuan wanted to continue, but Aunt Yuan couldn't stand it anymore. She scolded:

——Stop bragging, I think you really have no shame!

But the others were silent, each smiling in their own different ways; they knew that Uncle Yuan was strong, and his words wouldn't be false. But this glorious history of boasting was, after all, from the past! In recent years, that kind of situation has simply never happened. —Maybe it will never happen again?

A Teahouse Scene 212

— Qin Jian

In the season after spring has passed, the weather is gradually warming up: the clouds have a dark, heavy appearance, the leaves have a full, lush green of their prime, the streamside has the incessant croaking of frogs, and in the deep night's dreams there are red lotuses, and the people living in this warm current also have a kind of restless mood.

"Go search for the outside world!" Some people might have that kind of mood and go to a teahouse to steep a pot of tea, let it cool, wave a fan, and prop up their legs to watch the hustle and bustle of all kinds of people, to while away an early summer afternoon: but if you say that everyone who goes to the teahouse is suffering from indigestion, or has eaten too much and wants to use it to massage their overfull nerves, that can't be said to be entirely true. In the teahouse—even a small teahouse on the edge of a village next to a "tiger stove," people often gather there, bustling, arguing, discussing, lamenting all kinds of terrible, unpleasant problems in life, the restlessness and emotional disputes caused by the hard times, the fistfights caused by one or two silver coins; there, impatience, worry, resentment, sighs… the martial spirit of the heart mixes together, just like the mixing of countless different types of faces and different tones of voice.

Since the days of being a big child, in order to find a life buried at the end of the world, I have drifted far away from home for countless years. When I was young, I often saw the wandering flavor of foreign "gypsies" in the small teahouses in town; now that I've rekindled the memories of my childhood, and when I go to the teahouse, familiarly exchange four copper coins for a token and find a comfortable spot to sit down, the teahouse is no longer what it used to be.

The room is dark, with three or five rays of sunlight filtering in dimly. Several broken square tables are scattered around, people sit haphazardly on benches, talking haphazardly, arguing haphazardly. In the corner of the hall is still the broken wooden platform for singing folk songs, but no one is singing anymore, and no one has the leisurely mood to listen. People, with different faces, but with the same gaunt look, sweat dripping from their heads, uttering different sounds, looking at the walls and ceiling blackened by smoke and fire with pale eyes, but their minds are full of calculations and attempts: how to negotiate a small deal or two to buy rice, how to open their mouths to borrow three or five silver dollars to buy steamed buns, how to drag those who borrowed three or four cents of "usurious" interest from the annual government and use rough voices and strength to force them to repay. Face readers run around, putting up the sign of "skilled in observing expressions," greeting people with flattering smiles and formulaic jargon; but people, having lived in long-term displacement, have also learned to doubt fate. Even if someone really wants to know when there will be an end to the next hardship, they remember that the few copper coins in their pockets are still needed to live for another day, so they silently lower their heads, listening to the noise, insults, arguments, and fights of the people around them.

Who can say that the teahouse has a lovely hustle and bustle anymore—that should be a dream of the past. Now the teahouse still exists in the small village, but what is unfolding there is only the mortal combat of life and unhappiness.

They say: the teahouse is soft and sweet, but that is a thing of the past.

Spoken Drama 214

Guanyin Society

China (1140) 8:15 PM to 9:00 PM

"Modern Youth" After Zhou Jichun graduated from junior high school, Hong Shi urged Zhou Shiliang to formally present the betrothal gifts and held two tables of wine at home. However, Zhou Jichun and Jufeng were uncomfortable at home, so they went to the park together. Jichun drank a bottle of soda in the park and fell ill after returning home.

Movie News

Once a Year Beauty Queen 215

Before Wang Renmei entered the film industry, she was generally known as the "Beauty Queen." Since starring in the "Fisherman's Song" dubbed by Dentsu last year, it has been a full year since she parted ways with the audience. During this long year, she joined the mighty Dentsu. The fully voiced, singing feature film "Children of Wind and Cloud," which Dentsu will soon release, is the culmination of her efforts over the past year. With its poignant and magnificent content, and its plot of joys and sorrows, under the hard work of director Xu Xingzhi, it further unfolds the new acting skills of this "Beauty Queen." Once a year, we will see Wang Renmei's lively and abundant posture again.

Tang Na to Play the Male Lead in "City Scenery" 216

Tang Na, who came out of St. John's University the year before last to write film reviews, is now a screenwriter at Yihua Film Company. After completing the assistance in writing "Escape," he still had time. Recently, Dentsu hired him to play a male lead in Yuan Muzhi's "City Scenery," and he agreed to begin his new practice in film acting.

Tang Na, he has extensive film knowledge and is the most diligent film critic. He is also unusually qualified as an actor: a healthy physique, a handsome appearance, coupled with his rich scholarship and the help of a director who specializes in acting, this will surely open up a bright star future for him in addition to his many other achievements. This is probably good news that his literary lovers will be happy to know.

Microphone Broadcast 217

The third issue of the "Star Bi-Monthly" was published on schedule on the 15th. The cover photo of Gao Zhanfei and Gao Yiping facing each other is quite amusing.

Wu Suxin performed a drama with Chen Qiufeng in Wuxi for three days, creating quite a sensation.

In the second issue of "Female Students," Yuan Meiyun was said to live upstairs, and was named "Upstairs Miss."

The "National Soul," a great production by the Star Company, contains a song called "National Soul Song," which is quite majestic. Yesterday, more than a dozen musicians were specially invited to rehearse the score.

The Chinese Film Society has now established a National Library, with Ms. Zhou Diyun in charge. It is said that a deaf-mute film fan donated several hundred books, all about film.

Recently, several slippery companies have appeared in Shanghai that neither film nor act as introduction agencies. Film fans, don't be fooled!

The Star Photography Studio recently built a city scene, which is extremely grand. Some jokingly call it "Movie City."

It is reported that Hu Die and her husband Zhou Jianyun have already set off to return to the country yesterday and are expected to arrive in Shanghai in about three weeks.

Yihua Odds and Ends 218

Yuan Meiyun is sick, lying lonely in bed, not moving at all. Her face is so pale, her eyes so dull, her voice so low… Bitter tears flowed in her eyes, staring blankly at the ceiling, like being nailed to a wooden board and unable to move. ——"Storm" Yesterday, such a moving scene was filmed.

A large number of "prostitutes" perform in "Storm."

Is "Victory Song" working extremely hard these days?

The lead actor of Ya Yunwei's "Hero of the Times" has been selected, and a certain gentleman with a high reputation in the film industry will take the role. The name will be announced soon.

"The Beginning of Man" The scene where Wang Yin, who returned to China at the end, reads a letter from home on the ship, yesterday, director Dongshan, photographer Zhou Ke, and Wang Yin and others, a party of more than ten people, took a certain large ship sailing on the Yangtze River to Beijing. After the ship exited Wusongkou, this scene was filmed. After the ship arrived in Beijing, they transferred to the Beijing-Shanghai train to return to Shanghai, but Zhou Ke had to stay in Beijing for some time to lecture actors on photography techniques at the Central Photography Studio.

Han Langen Almost Played a Monk Getting Married 219

Han Langen was originally supposed to shave his head for the role of Xiao Baba in "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp," but the filming coincided with his wedding date. It would have been too much to have him marry his new wife with a shaved head, along with her dazzling veil, so the director had to change the script slightly to accommodate him. However, that concession came with a condition: he had to kowtow three times to his new wife in front of the partygoers on his wedding night and go to the photography studio to film the next day.
